O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, three sons, I have fulfilled this book that is behind the science of medicine the fulfillment of it, and made the end through its exposures and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I came to my mind that I have fulfilled this with the cautery, which is from hands' work, it is known as "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is troubled in our region and is neglected in every way, if it is perished by science and knowledge, and there is nothing left but the small descriptions in books written by the ancients that the hands have seen.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And this has led to the error and ignorance, and the intentions are closed and the science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I will live it together by assembling the order of this cauterization according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will assemble the forms of the fire-cautery instruments and other tools of the work with the assistance of the declaration and preparation of the one, as he is skilled.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled hands masters are found in our time, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who enters the science of anatomy, as Galen says, must know the judgment of the members, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of the parts, and have knowledge of the bones, nerves, and teeth, and the number of joints, and the movement and resting of the limbs, and the fruit of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Iocras says that the non is not with the non and with the wrist is little; and moreover in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the introduction of this book, we say that those who are not knowledgeable in these things should be warned, lest they make errors and harm men; for I have often seen many of these who become involved in this science and abandon it and its science and experiment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I see a man who cuts off the testicle of a woman or the col of her neck, and cuts into the arteries of the col; because so much blood flows out that the woman dies in her own hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And see another case where a wound on a man's body was treated, and the wound was large; if it was removed with a piece of the bladder, and he died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I have already been called upon to treat this wound, and I see the position of the helper and the size of the wound, and if it was not cut well, it would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see another case where a man of our land, who had a broken leg, was treated with the aid of a splint and plaster; and the surgeon was greatly praised for closing the break on the bone as quickly as possible, without leaving any part of the bone exposed, and he finally terminated the treatment; and he commanded that the leg not be moved; and later, when the leg was completely healed and the piez, it came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called to come to him, and I hurried to come limb-by-limb; and when I see it dislocated, if it is not painful and does not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of the corruption were already confirmed or member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop spreading through the member as long as the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another mirror that will fall and be enchanted, and then inflamed by the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is free of melancholic humor, only then does it happen that if it is not in part the limb can be completely healed what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	1. For this reason, thrice-woven threads, you should know that work of hands is divided into two divisions: it is skill, whether or not there is risk in other dispositions; and I will show each thread of this book where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	2. For this reason, keep your threads safe, so that the enemy cannot speak ill of you. Take your weapons in hand and use them lightly but firmly, and use the best way possible for the grace of God to save you and make you healthy; and let the unwholesome diseases of grief be cured; and keep your weapons in such a way that you do not doubt their power, and have faith in them so that you can come from this world to another with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiens warn in several of their admonitions: "Do not take false remedies for your illness, so that you are not called foolish.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have found this treatment in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medicinal cauterizations, and it orders the chapters from the head down to the feet; as well as forms of strangulations, and forceps for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and pricking, and ventouses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it orders the chapters and forms of strangulations.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered by the main chief, and the forms of the stones.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	However, if we remember our work, it is necessary that I give the quality of the aid and no harm to any complexity.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and no harm, is the longest word and subtlest science and the secret remedy; and for this they speak more of wounds, and agree on this; and they are short in their words because I repeat the long words.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally with any complexion or matter, for every complexion: it's to know hot complexions with much matter, and dry complexions with much matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions, they say cauterization does nothing and that it is great help; the other says the opposite: that cauterization is only good for diseases that come from chill and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of hot fire is hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from chill, nor by dryness; and that is what the one who says the opposite says, that cauterization helps greatly with hot diseases that come from the courage of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you perceive the heart of the patient and its moisture on the complexion, you know the heart is burning.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I concur with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it before by experiment.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all paths, it interferes with the least as those who have experienced it and know the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their symptoms and the spaciousness of tens; other complexions do not have our experience, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And they were found to resemble and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Understand, children, that cauterization is similar to fire if it is a secret of the arts, and above all, it is an ardent medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and it only causes harm to the member that is cooked, and does not harm other members.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The ardent medicines come from one member to another by removing, and they bring the maladies of grief to the healthy state; and by chance, if the fire has too much heat and good substance, it does not cause harm, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	1. And I found this in my experiments and through the service I have provided and the study I have conducted in the art, and it is true; and for this I apologize for the length of the word, because I only want to reveal to you the secret that is inside or fire, and the quality of the work, as it affects the diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says by demonstrating; and you should receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	1. Understand, son, that the cauters should be made in such a way that they are appropriate, and they should be pried.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	1. I say that the cautery is useful in all cases because the wounds are not well placed by the help of the cautery; and at the same time, if the cautery is for necessary pains and hastens that cannot wait for the time that greatest malice does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think that the cure is easy, like the physician's; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and he says so; but it is not so if one takes care, because cauterization is only a medicine that dries up the complexion, and dries up the humors that cause the pain, and is as good as medicine for hastening one's courage, and for one's virtue and nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	However, there is a thing that the disease does not recur again according to the complexion of the patient and the humors of the disease, and they are assembled in him, the superfluities, through the acquisition of meat and such things, unless cauterization is administered to him or he has little superfluity and moisture, like cauterization for toothache, and the humors, and only a part of the pain returns; but this does not happen often.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	1. And many people do not understand why cauterization is called surgery by some, but it is seen; however, they only believe that cauterization is effective after medicine, but we understand that it is false, and it is called surgery because when we administer remedies for any disease and they are not effective, we then use cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	2. Therefore, it is well that cauterization is called surgery, but not according to the attention of fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	3. The ancients said that a gold cauterization instrument was as harmful as one made of iron, and they said this because of the quality of the gold and the high content of its substance; and they said that gold cauterization did not cause any poisoning, but it is not true because I have experienced it and found that it is true in some men; and gold cauterization is as good as iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	When you hold the gold instrument, you do not know if it is hot by its color, and it has cooled down; and if you heat it too much, it will melt; so be careful with fire.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that is why we use fire cautery in our work, because it has been proven to be effective.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have ordered this chapter of the little finger nails, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Olive oil cautery is used on moist and cold hands, and it is done for the disease called "soda," and for many humors that descend from the little finger as ears, and eyes, and numerous sleeplessness and toothache and throat pain, and also for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and semblances of disease.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is as follows: if the patient is purged by medicine that alters the crown III or IV, according to what the virtues and the age and the accustomed habits of the patient can bear; then repeat the dose of the medicine for the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then place the root of your palm between the root of his thumb and index finger; then if you have two means, either squeeze or wash the cauterization called "oliva" which is formed as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put ink on the flesh, and make it descend and tighten your hand repeatedly, then relax your hand slightly, and reward the finger if you see the bone move a little; if you do not see it, continue the cauterization as long as you see the bone as I told you; then take the gauze, and wet it with saliva, and put it on the finger, and let it lie for three days; then wet the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" as soon as it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if the ancients said that the more tense the wound is, the more it discharges; and this is because it helps to heal.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And no one of these says that you should stretch the cauterization so much that part of the bone is raw, and then remove what is raw of the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the cauterization should be stretched as much as possible, and if one presses too hard, it may cause the bone to break wide like a vessel because the humors flow out; and after this, it should be treated and soothed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	1. These two methods of cauterization do not seem to be the best in any way, despite their being used by many men or those who fear; and I think that I should leave them alone, as the heads of the shoulder are weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have experienced in other parts; and even when the head of the shoulder is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems to be more salve and less painful for me, and therefore I use it in this way.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	1. of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	1. When the entire head is in chronic pain and lasts for a long time, if one must use the drugs called "cochie" and pills, as well as purification of the head and oils and plasters; and if it is done as we have described before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	The patient's head is of great nature and should not be too tight; therefore, the cauterization is done on that part we have mentioned earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each corne of the head, as we have mentioned before, and then cauterizing the lower part of the eye called "vassels"; and they are those that are placed with ventouses; and hold your hand so you do not see the bone: the patient feels too much pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will explain later; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the corneas be more sensitive than those of the lower part of the eye, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the body there is sudden pain, and it spreads throughout the disease, and the patient is purged with medicines that modify the oil, and the other treatments I have mentioned in the division of diseases are not effective: therefore, I made the cauterizations in two ways, that is, with medicinal ointment and with iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	If you apply a poultice of ointment and the wound comes out and becomes crusted, and then you make a temple or hold the part in such a way that you can pour the ointment of the wound; and when it is poured, if the patient holds the lip and draws it well and leaves it for 12 hours; then the lip is removed and the dressing is applied with the plaster, leaving the wound for 2 or 3 days; then you put the whole hand in water until it becomes moist.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of inflammation when it is healed; and if you see that there are no such medicines as I have written or treated of any harmful medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron burn is according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron burner so that it has this form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc. de emigraine	of embolism
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre. de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere. After pressing the fistula, it becomes overstretched, and the matter is drained and dried; if it opens, and the bowel follows, after cutting the burned cautery, and place your hand on the cautery at the part where the fat is not greasy, so that your hands do not slip; and place the cautery in the fat of the oil, and it corrodes.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization at the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then renew the cauterization again, and if you have experience with it, and leave it for three days; after that, place cotton wool on the dressing, and apply the dry ointment as soon as it is clean, and when forty days have passed and it is clean, if you apply an acidic corrosive medicine to the bone until it is discovered; and follow according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing fistulas that no ancient ones knew.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understands the fistula, and then put in the forceps I have a subtle cord of copper:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the amount of a .З. of plonc; and hold your hand firmly with the forceps, and do not move the patient at all, only the ploncs will be absorbed into their oil; and it is necessary to put the oil on clean cotton wool in the corner of the eye or in the ear: the ploncs if they are near the fistula, and the patient will be healthy in health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer purgatives to the newborn, and bring the fistula back to the center of the umbilicus according to what is appropriate for the specific case.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are cracks in the lips that are called "splits," and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks according to what we have described in divisions, and the patient does not benefit, then use a small cauterization tool according to this form:

de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the gall
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms in the gallbladder or uterus, or in the roots of the teeth, and it becomes inflamed and forms a fistule; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit: therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize according to the size of the fistule; after the bite or rupture of the fistule, and hold your hand until the fire comes out of the wound, and if it is inside the limb; and then make once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, as soon as it is healthy; and if it is cured once or twice, it is good; and if not, you must discover the limb and open the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines and it does not work, then put a poultice of bad herbs on your gum; after that, wash the cautery that came from this part in this way, so that you put a cord around the tooth; and remove the teeth from the cautery as quickly as possible, and hold your hand tightly with the bad pain coming from the root of the tooth; then gently release your hand and continue the cautery according to your will; then fill the bad herbs in your mouth with rotten flesh, and chew it for an hour and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gum becomes soft and restrained, and the moisture is dried out and becomes hard.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from cold, or it is cold or visible, and the remedies of medicine do not work, then there is need for cauterization in two ways: and cauterization with a burr and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with a burr if it is such that you use a sheep’s wool burr and the end in a iron or copper cup; then take cotton and wrap around the point of a needle, and make it burrowed in the painful tooth as much as it is cold; and often I do this until the virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton are burned in the burr, and put on the painful tooth and put on the iron chair as much as the flesh reaches to the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	1. When the fire cautery is used, if it is as hot as a hound of iron or fire, and is large enough to reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cautery, shape it according to this, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often because the pain will be eased for either the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	2. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with a hard ball in the pressure of this cautery, and then releases it; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cut as you wish, according to what you have to; and this is the form of the knife:
des scrophules	of scrophulous tumors
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophulous tumors are soft and cold, and do not respond to digestion with medicines, then clean the scalpel of the knife after it comes out of the form, and make two openings for the smoke to issue from the other side; and place the scalpel on the abscess once, or as it is fit, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the scalpel according to the amount of pus, and leave it there for three days; and wrap the wound with damp cloth as soon as the wound oozes; afterwards cure the wound with purges and ointments as soon as it is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the collar:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistors enter the throat, and at the same time when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must be treated first with soluble medicines; after that, I perform a fire cautery at the base of the chin, and make sure you do not go too deep into the chin, and only burn a little bit.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, I perform another cautery at the joint of the shoulder and the head of the spine, and it is called the "clavicle"; and cure the limb as we have said, so long as it is healthy.

de l’enfleure des piez	of the enflaming of the wounds
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the wounds are enflamed by the humid, and are plain yellowish, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of it between the auricular and the anusular, and gently hold the cauterization with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too much in front, otherwise the patient's skin will be burned, and the cauterization should be done according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two cauterizations on each leg at the cuticular point; and the cauterization should be long, one in front of the genital area and the other behind, along the leg; and leave the cauterizations to heal for as long as necessary, according to the patient's condition; after the cure of the other cures that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the menstruation
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the abdomen comes from cold and moisture, as long as the digestive and vitals that are in the stomach and intestines are distended, and cannot be cured by any means of cures; and you see the patient very suffering and of strong greenish color, if I make a large cauterization on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before or on the stomach, at the cauterization circle; and four cauterizations are made around the bowels subtly, at all the cauterization clavicle subtle, and two cauterizations are made on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see much moisture and the patient is suffering, make the fire cautery on the point, and the cautery on each side, and the cauteries on the stomach below the great belly button, because the cure is beneficial when it has good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are either fundament or one or more, and are old and large humors cold and moist corrupted, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and if they do not profit, if you make cauterizations: III on the spine of the back, which is all deformed and bent, and the cautery on the anus II doses; and if you think that the stomach is cold, and the meat is not cooked, and the face swells, then the face on the greatest cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and the other on the liver, and the other on the gallbladder at all the cauteries clamped; and leave the cauterization over long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the wound has healed to the point of being healthy.

de plaie mal curee	of a badly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere. When there is no fistula, and it is awake and has sweat and putrid milk, if you provide enough of this subtle tent, and make sure to hold the entire tent as much as it has to.

se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	1. If the fistula is in the course of the vein and the intestine, and these are made only in the testicle, and believe that it is not a rare thing; after healing the testicle as much as it is healthy, and if the leus is removed, and the materials are long bones, then heal that the testicle is completely healthy; and if the materials are long bones, heal that the testicle is entirely healthy, and if the materials are not bones, heal that the testicle is missing, and corroded the bone at its root.
de la maladie des reins	The disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide. de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is full and weak due to kidney stones and moisture, if the patient retains urine, then you should cauterize in the part where the urethra meets the bladder, on both sides, and so on for each; and you should also cauterize the back of the bladder, or the other side; and so the cauterizations should be made according to the form mentioned before.

de la hainche	The second sentence to translate is "de la hainche

de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the chest

When pain comes in the chest, and it is cold and moist, and the patient is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure is not effective, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of large humors with bitter pills or other bone-like pills.

And if you see, if the cauterization is done at the circle we mentioned in the dislocation of the thorn; but do it in a different way that the circles contain the entire thorn, and all its points no matter how small they are.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	This is the manner in which one treats sciatica, when the pain remains in the buttock and does not reach the thigh or leg.

Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is in the groin and goes towards the thigh, then cauterize with a circular or cutting cautery, and be careful with all your cauterizations that you do not burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause further harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés. de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by touching or drumming or from too much evacuation, or from the expansion of cold matter, none of these appearances warrants cauterization, rather it is for the one who has come from the infusion of cold matter.
