Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the head of this very subtlety, and the tail in third angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the cheek and the nose.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No time are born or grown without cheeks, and if there are any that seem to have scorpions at the mouth of the face; and if they have an enhanced cheek with a different color, and if it has a cheek with a natural color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that of these cheeks which are not enhanced, and do not have an enhanced cheek, it is necessary that you put the mustache between your hands before the sun; and work on the nostrils, and moisten the snout with those cheeks, and pull them out; so that you can hold it steady at the subtle tip of a spatula, as long as you see that this cheek is all grown.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, if you examine all the surgical instruments lightly and subtly, without causing any harm; and if it does not overwhelm you, or cause an abscess, if it is a malignant one, then quickly cauterize it as much as possible until it is not inflamed and all the bones are charred, then cool it with water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you operate, and moisture comes to the palace, which is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, which is charred in the bone of the limb, or the instruments cannot be cut: therefore it is necessary that you tie a thread around the end of the linen, which is large enough for your hands, and it must be between every nail and the docket or less; and put the sharp edge of the other end of the mallet in the child's mouth, and let it odor until it comes out through the nose; and often make the child perform this exercise, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the first finger that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other finger that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and follow it after the other.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Do as much as you can see that the child has corrupted the char, then take the boy's penis, clean the wound, and wipe the boy's penis with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the urethra as before; do this 3 to 4 times, until the ointment corrodes all that is left of the char; then put a piece of cork in the urethra for as long as it is healthy, and if you have experience with drying herbs, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the child's penis, or when you distill the oils and medicines or the urine:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hanging lamp, like a candelabrum, and it is led thus; and if you see, if a candle is closed, and it is the extinguishers plain for expelling the fire; and it has an arm to hold the head when one heats the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	and of the sword when the need arises.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times it is seen at the head of a disease called "telul", which grows and becomes large, until it is seen as something to be looked at; and for this it is necessary to cut at the beginning, and all the bone, then put the cautery or the hot medicine; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of dark color, poor sense: if it does not touch any iron because it is enchanted, since when one touches it never, if evil comes to the patient; and if the apostemas are touched, not of dark color, and you see that it can be covered, if the patient is empty and the apostema is touched without pain, and cure the patient of things that are dry and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the joint is cut and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when a solution for continuation comes from one of these cartilages, it does not last long, and this is true in no man's land.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to do this if no one has come beforehand; and then look at whether the wound is fresh at all its base; and then treat it with a bandage, as soon as it is safe; and if the lips are already swollen on both sides, then remove all the parts of them that are sick, and then assemble the lips with a bandage, and extract, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and burn incense; and put on the powder a piece of an emplaustre of some other emplauster, and leave it as long as it is dry, then treat the ointment as soon as it is safe.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	1. The method of sewing is as follows: whether you use needles or thread, as we have mentioned in the abdominal stitching; or by hand, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	2. of lip sutures
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. de la char des gencives	Of the thigh of the knee
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the thigh of the knee has been burned, which they call "albulus"; if you can hold it with your nails, and the root with the foot, and let go of the vein or the sinus; then put on vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccant powders; and if the thigh returns after the incision, and many times it happens, if the root is second time, and cauterized; if it does not return soon after the cauterization; and these are the forms of the estrumens with the copper.
des sordens	of the scars
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are gathered at the jaws, jaws between the cheeks, ulcers that are harsh and sharp; and no times is the black and yellow and pointed tooth, until corruption comes to the cheek, and it becomes the blackened tooth; if you come to place the mouth between your hands, and its chips are in your holy hand, and open the jaws or ulcers as long as there is nothing more; and then I make black and green, and yellow and other stains, as they are turned; and if this is in the first reason, it is good; but if not, then renew the second day and the tooth, as you have everything turned; and you should know that the teeth have different forms of gums to laugh, according to what the tooth demonstrates, because the raser that rubs the teeth has other shapes than those that are shown between the teeth; and these forms and others are with you visible.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the patient's pain that you delay treating as much as possible and as quickly as you can, because it should not be otherwise; for it is a substance of high value therefore there is no excuse for neglecting it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is confined to bed, if you are certain that they have pain, then.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient's pain has passed, and it is necessary to keep the patient warm and give them to drink; and until the patient is completely recovered, for these are the most dangerous times; and when you are certain that the patient has pain, if you must scratch the skin of the entire body, then first do it gently at all points; then pull out the hairs with your nails; and place the patient's head between your knees and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth sharply with forceps, and if it does not break, then take none of these hooks and gently pull out from each side, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the teeth are felt and pulled out, then it is necessary to fill them with cloth, wherever there are holes; and if the extraction is done subtly with hooks, it will not break the tooth; and it is wise to overturn the gum for cleaning the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you should be very careful not to break it, and there will remain a part, and the patient suffers from the malice of the root, greater pains in the first place.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should wear this to avoid causing pain like those who ignore health, who through their haste and their audacity break the charm never, and do not cause pain to anyone that we have known; but they bring it once by the agony of this great disease from its roots that they do not want, or from the bone that they break, just as often as we have wanted; and when it is cold, if you wash the skin with wine or vinegar and salt; and if they dislocate and come out, which often happens, if you use the skin of vitriol, and if it does not work, if it cauterizes.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the tooth-grinders, whether they are still or not, are long and wide at the tips and large in size, and they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they be of large members if they do not break when pulled out, and they be well-made iron, and they be teeth to hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth becomes loose, if it comes to pass that you put your thumb on the gum for an hour or more.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the root is smooth, if it remains so, you pull out the points called "algefris," of which the heads appear to be like a beard; and they be made thus also like a wedge and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out through all these pricks, then it comes that you dig out the whole of the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", which is a type of tweezer, and its form is like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very thick and does not break the skin, and the root jumps through this, it is good; but if not, then use all the forceps, and the forms come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you help with this instrument that has two prongs, its form is like this:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And of other forceps that are before in the reason of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like large thorns, its form is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	1. And so it is that the joint will not break, and the tools are sharp; and others are made of denser materials; and the masters are skilled in using their own instruments according to what they observe in their patients' conditions, because they have diseases that are not taught by the diversity of instruments used by different times, or break due to other bones, or cause other parts to fracture, if they seek estruments that are suitable for the joints I mentioned, and guide you with gestures, as shown in the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	2. And let them be large and well-grasped to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can hold and support it; then restore the leu of the medicines suitable for this, and if there is inflammation in the bone, and it is small, then use all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears that does not fit with the natural corporeal form, and its shape is deformed, and at the same time in women, if it is necessary to remove it after the tooth, and it is not true that it is there, and it cannot be soaked or limed: therefore the root; and if it is found with the tooth, if this instrument whose form is shown here is taken, and it resembles a small beak, and is made of iron very sharp:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the force is little by little with the hands years due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be limed, then the liming of a part of the liming as shown here is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	1. And it comes as if the lime is made like the goggles; and in the lime the beak is very small and small in the hands, so that it does not move at all until it chicks; then the flatness at the end has no rasping, and the tongue is too sharp and it bends the tongue, if it manages to emasculate as much as it can be equal, so that it does not bend the tongue and does not corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	2. When the beak is dislocated.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	3. When the beak is dislocated in front by pressure or by blow, and the patient cannot press on it as he wants to, and you should treat him with restraining medicines, and it does not work; if it is restrained by a golden thread, because the silver threads become green and slimy, but the gold does not move at all; and if the thread is too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of the spice between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take a golden thread and a silver thread double between the healthy teeth, then put the threads between the diseased teeth, as long as you see sagacity in the healthy tooth; then resume the covering on the part where you started, and gently and wisely stretch your hand, so that it does not move at all; and if your finger is at the root of the tooth, so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then, put the teeth into the bone, assemble them, and re-insert them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not chip the tongue; then, leave it as tight as possible and let it stay, or if it comes out, if the thread snaps, then the other thread will be pulled; if it stays and holds all its tension, and is the form of the teeth and the shape of the incisors of the second teeth and the second premolars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is reset in its place, it must be done carefully, as we have said; and it should not be forced if it is not sharp and painful, and never made to look like a bone tooth of a mare, and it is placed on the gum where it was deformed, and it is tightened as we have said, and it should not be forced, and held in place:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Of the copper wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Never is a wire that comes out of the tongue or nature, that one makes in it; or by accident of wound; and the ovraiges are such that you make the mouth of the midwife, and it has its head in your hand, and relaxes the tongue; then cope the nervous wires that are large, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it becomes hard or out, and this is due to wounding, if the tooth bites it and cope large, the other one; and keep that the fever does not become too much, for the artery that is out; and when you have done, if the tongue is red and sore, or cold, then put back in its place a tent of linen; and the midwife will tease the patient every night, that the one who uses it can soothe.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the dislocation occurs, if the patient does not immediately grasp the leg with vitriol, and if it is not possible to cauterize at the slow cauterization point that is suitable for this, then the other treatment begins as soon as it is safe.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, and it is not touched, because it is a gangrene; and if it is declining into a bladder, and it is moist, and the wound is oozing, and it is cleaned with a subtle sponge, and the discharge is from one side and another; and if it is not possible to reach your goal, then immediately grasp it with vitriol as soon as it is inflamed, and return to your goal as soon as you have dealt with everything; then lift the leg of silk and thread, and the other treatments as soon as it is safe.
des apostemes de la gorge	gums of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes the gums of the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "amandines". When you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, then keep them: if they are hard and small in size and color, and not sharp like iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, and not sharp like iron, then it is due to blood; but it will remain so until it is dead, and then you will take it out; and if it is of a watery color and the root is subtle, and you have prepared the instrument with care, but first look to see if the gums are calmed and settled.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, and his head be in your hand, and he opens the mouth and the tongue between his hands, and presses the langue so tight to all the instrument, of whatever it may be, whether silver or gold: and it is as if some counterweights.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue so tight to all this instrument, and see the incision, if you take the icepick and the needle in the hare, and draw it as far as you can; and take no other thing with you, then the copes of the instrument, of whatever it may be, that seems like forces; and all the chief are crossed, and one place the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if it is sharp, then the form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And so, one part should be cut and the other named; and when you cut one of the hairs, cut the other in the same manner, and after making the incision, warm the sharp blade with hot water, and make it sharp and smooth, and if the blood comes out, if the blade is heated, or if burns from pomegranate peels are cooled, or if fuelled mirte, and similar things, as long as they are not bleeding; then the cure is done when it is healthy; and no other styphlus ever appears in the mouth except the two hairs of the II amandres, if they are cut like the II amandres.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess in her throat that was causing pain, which is known as an "aposteme of little sensation"; she had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe out through the clogged passageway, and could not drink or eat, and died if she lingered for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been opened twice by the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I thought to cut the abscess open, and found a great portion of bowels inside; then I cut into another opening, and opened the woman's mouth and pressed on her tongue; after cutting the abscess in these places, and taking out a piece, there was only a little blood; and then she was able to swallow water and wine, and began to drink more and more, and the abscess continued to grow larger, filling the part I had cut; the abscess finally burst open, and filled the hole that I had made, so that it grew very large; then I cauterized the abscess in the throat: afterwards she recovered, and I left these parts, and only God knows what happened after me.
de l’uve	Of the urethra
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the urine flows into the urethra, and it is narrow and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and rounded, it is called "urethra".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, you see that the incisions are calmed and subtle, and if you touch it, it is suitable; and the one that is rounded and not long is assembled and not far; and it is bloody or has a fuscous color or black, and if you expel the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For it poses great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, as I have said, to follow the manner I described, with regard to the patient's belly and length, that you place the midwife before the sun, and press the tongue onto the instrument we made note of earlier; then cut the umbilicus, and draw it out, and sew it in two segments as I mentioned in the incision of the two umbilical cords.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too much beyond the natural end, for if you do, it will cause strain on your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two umbilical cords, and cure it as soon as it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	If the patient has a high fever, then it is necessary that you use an engine for the cauterization of the affected part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is to make it hot and dry.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the patient puts his head in your hand and then presses his tongue on the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confines it with hot, dry fire, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and then uses the edge of this instrument, its form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a lock of hair or puts medicine in his mouth, as one does with a tooth, and places the instrument at all the medicine on the eyeball; and the patient is gasping for air, if the saliva and mucus are coming from his mouth due to the medicine given, if it does not reach the throat and neck, then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the eyeball, as much as you can see the narcissism and the pain of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and pull the instrument through all the cotton in the tail of the cord, as much as the cotton dries on the eyeball; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and wait after four or five hours or five days, and if you have the skill to re-cauterize the medicine, if it resumes, and after cauterizing the discharge around the eyeball, wrap it in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and use gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision, only burning; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take mustard, soap, and sage, chamomile, thyme, and rosemary, and all or none of them in one pot, and mix, and boil; and it can be well glued with strong earth, and the pot should have the comb according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be of silver or gold, and one of the heads is put into the patient's mouth as long as the vapor rises through the urethra, until the urethra is hardened; afterwards, it resumes often, until the urethra is dry, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of gangrene, because many things come; and do not make this too early in the decline of gangrene.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a needle and sew the corner of the eye with a thread, if the eye does not have too much inflammation; for the thread does not harm the eyeball, and it is a good cure in assembly salute.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened in the throat, or with a bone of fish, or nothing at all; if it comes then that you see what you need to see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and if you do not open it and it is stuck in the throat, then it is necessary to make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it is made clear by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of gauze, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and then put it on the sponge and then glutinate; and when it comes to the mouth, if it slips, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out of what we have said, then take the instrument of punch according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the strap be placed on the head if it can more gently enter the mouth, and the head be raised up; and watch that you do not touch the epigastrium, that all may not vie, nor the bone be bent; and it is best that the patient and the instrument be held, because it is most suitable or the thing is there; if it is held, or it is drawn further along the entire instrument evenly, as far as it goes.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's loose skin
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never has medicine been used on loose skin, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not profit, then look at the mouth of the patient's face towards the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the shoulder, if the bone is all in one piece, or if it has thin hairs that are worth nothing in this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth anything, then take a hair from the head of a woman, and tie it around the neck of the patient, and then pull or cut off the hair, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient's scalp is sweating all the time.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full advantage of the cool sweat on your face, and open your mouth, and feel the saliva enter your throat often; and if the shoulder feels hot, then do this.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If the patient does not understand as we have said, if the cauterizer smokes a lot of asafetida, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, as it will feel better.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation if you prefer to use or if there are charcoal pieces, and it is the head covered with a cloth in the environment, and in the other part, the head of the instrument; then do your fumigation, and the cauterizer puts the tip of the snake's tail in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not enter, but goes to the throat; and the throat will now hurt, and if it hurts again, do the fumigation many times; and let the cauterizer be thirsty, and drink salty and acidic things, and do not drink lemon water; and then do your work as it was done by this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat the wound, if it is, when it can be seen, resembles tinea corbicularis with sharp points that can enter the mouth; it looks like a beak of a surgeon, and has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it touches, it cannot let go; and this is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of the sutures
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of the sutures are, according to which memory comes after another in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is in its own appearance similar, and for that it is moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is if the limbs are lying down or at rest.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the head of the chief is different from that of the foundation, and the head of the lower limb is different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if one cannot perceive the head, as long as the bow is dead according to its completion; and if there are such cases where it must be perceived when it is believed, and they do not die until their completion, then like those that are difficult to reach in joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when the head comes from difficult joints, and it is left as long as it is dry, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the abscess cure, if it is located on the principal limb, and you delay the puncture as long as possible before it bursts, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is located in the foundation, and you do not stop until it bursts, then it will be like a digestion completed in vain, just like the one that is located in the foundation, which will not close, and will become a fistula; and it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure. En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that are pricked, according to the pain of the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is formed in the member, if it is painful, then you should leave the puncture until it is confirmed to be well digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick it in this way, if the blood comes out of it, and it is painful to look at, and by chance hardens the lips and makes them crooked; and then endurances the face.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is felt according to the pain of the member, then it should be left according to the size of the blood.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	The text is asking the reader to carefully and accurately remove small buttons, buttons, and numerous stitches according to the size of the button; and if there are such buttons or stitches that are too large, they should be cut off. When it becomes as soft as I am, and is worn out, it is necessary to make them in the same way as bubbles: and if there are such ones that are cut at three angles, and if there are such ones that are cut like the thorn of a rose, like buttons of anger; and if there are such ones that are made into a larger size, and other sizes and appearance are also cut.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	The first line of the text translates to: "Those who lack a head, just like an abscess on the surface, it is necessary that you open it gradually; and when the abscess is large, and the pus is thick, and you open it, unless you drain all the pus in that hour, but only a part of it, then the abscess closes up to the other side, then you do not touch anything else; you do this many times, as long as the pus is all gone; at the same time, if the patient is weak in virtue, or a woman carries, or children are small, or old people are feeble.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectoration there is no time with the issue of the bowel, that by chance dies the patient, and you do not blame yourself.

Then the bone, and the care of ointment as soon as it is healthy.

And if the evacuation of blood persists, if it is governed and treated, and the powders I mentioned in my hands are in this book, and if you have pain, and the wound is nervous, then you should put on warm clothes and moisten your skin with wine and olive oil; and if this is the case, and the wound is charred, then you should put on cold water and olive oil, or wine and oil, as soon as possible, according to what we have said; and then close the wound and dress it, according to what is necessary.

des scrophules	The first sentence to translate is "des scrophules

Often, the wound of the abscess is at the collarbone, and the stitches come out, and the skin becomes inflamed, and never once do they go to another part or close, and they become infected, and one bone is connected to another.

In the position that you see of good arrangement at the edge, and resembles the color of the strong arm, and quiet in every part and not like any other pain or artery or conduit, and not like any other; if it comes that you cut it with a knife, and burn in every part, and are the lips of the knee as the bones, if you have the skill, as we have said in apostles, and the scar is small and few, and you are sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and are not like the salt that the hands do not protect, that the eyes see too soon, that you do not;

si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it, and dig further, and cut as we have said.

de squinance	Of the shoulder
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the shoulder's size; however, I have never seen anyone do it in our time, and this is the scripture of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with dislocation, it is necessary that the shoulder wound called "epiglottis" be avoided; and none can help with this, because all wounds and the patient's pain are in those who have lost consciousness in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the other members.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat, it is necessary to close the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	1. It is therefore necessary, when we wish to cut the epigastric region, that we cut it in three or four circles or five small cuts passing through the two circles or according to the quantity of the cut, and not in the cartilage; and this is sufficient for the section of the epigastric region without causing pain, and the wounds are long enough to be stitched.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	2. And if the masters are poor, then it comes to pass that the gullet of the neck is extended all the way to the throat, and then cut as far as the chin; and avoid the veins of the face, if you see nothing, and then cut the flesh, as we have said; and is demonstrated by the section of the swelling of the chin that it would have been torn apart by the neck which is broken, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed since it was set, gather the two lips of the wound as much as possible, and touch all parts of the cartilage; then administer medicines that make the patient feel better, until they are healthy again.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim does not do anything until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is near death, and the lack of air is fatal.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore, it is recommended to operate on the epigastrium because the patient cannot breathe, and they are breathing through the wound, and it should be guarded against death; and that is why the ancients ordered the wound to remain over the bone as long as the malice of the disease had not passed, and it had passed after three days or four. And therefore, it was ordered to cut the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured; and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a maiden is hurting her throat, and she bites on the gauze, and parts of her fur are coming out; and I was called to cure her, and I found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound, and I find the blood that came out of it, and though she had no veins or it led further than just the throat, it was due to the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened to care for the wound and cure it as soon as she was healed; and she did not come back for the maiden until her voice was hoarse, and she returned later in her place; therefore I say that there is no pain in the epigastrium.
de la grosse gorge	Of the large mouth
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien. des nous	The first sentence to translate is
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of us, which I will mention all the appearances; and it comes that I make all the difference between newborn and born.

The manner of incising abscesses of the body is that you prick or make it wetter than the abscess you are opening, and turn your two points a little at a time until you see that the stitch has caught the keur, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the dislocating instrument, and hold tight while you jump.

Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi. de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the tooth
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is ever born without having a fever in the tooth, or if the fever is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is too much to perceive at all, not even with the most delicate sensation, according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close. Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the catheter is small, if it is treated with a tight clot, as we have said, if it stretches.

Those who do not have the catheter in their groin are bleeding, because no one is born with a catheter at the top of the thigh, for they cannot urinate before they cut off their thigh; and they cannot enjoin because of this, because the matter cannot come out just yet, and it is a serious illness.

des pustules de la verge	2. of the pustules of the scalpel
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	3.
