de la circoncision	Of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a major wound if it is similar to others; however, when we perform this work out of our own will and for the benefit of our children, and in fact, it is the best work we can do and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not call circumcision of their children because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the greatest part of the masters and physicians who performed circumcision inside the dial, and had force and at all ages; if it were possible to know, it would be better than having many toiles, and by chance, if one wants to do that of another, and moreover, if it is done without force.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the wound is cleaned, and there is double pain, and to the circumcision which is not securely held, the point of the painful member; and to the circumcision of the finger by chance escapes the iron, and cuts the skin, and many times grow again because they have no skill in circumcision and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the circumcision which is made with force, I have found the benefit of the experiment because the forces cut both sides of the thread equally as well as without it.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if it cuts equally on both sides; but that the thread should be well twisted around the nail; and that the first dislocation is done in such a way that the child does not think he is being hurt, only that you are tying the thread around the finger so that he can see, and then tie it in all the ways you can think of; then you put your hand on the finger and blow on it or keur, and raise it as high as the head of the finger is assembled, then mundify well the dirt that is gathered there, then tie a double knot of the thread, then tie the other end to the other lien; and you hold it in place by the second reading in the pouch and the dot index, and cap between the two liens, then gently pull on the keur handle and raise the head of the finger; then let the sanc poc and poc, because it is the worst part; and put some powder on it and dust it with some powder from a cooked beef cut in slices, pickled in red wine, and fried, and leave it sus jusc’a the other jor, and the cure of another cure as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the mummification is this: the two heads are flat and thin, and are as strong as the fingers.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the skin comes out at the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend it along your finger, unless the flesh is gangrene; and it should be done properly, and if you do not hold it with your finger, then the skin.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and the wound is in a state of gangrene, if you allow it to be so that the gangrene does not become aggravated, and lightly burn it; if the skin is as you hold it from the part of the wound, it will not hurt you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The first sentence to translate is: "Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s'on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	If urination is difficult due to cystitis, or gallstones, or bowels, or a bowel obstruction, or similar things, that we mentioned in the division; and if urine is not passed, and you see the retention at the urethral opening, which is at the top or bottom of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his side, and his abdomen is expanded from the part below the loins, and the abdomen is restricted as much as possible; and then the patient's lower abdomen is compressed at the urethral opening to prevent the passage of urine, and if it does not pass, and as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary that you apply an extraction with all the instruments called "siringue", and its form is: a fine silver thread, like the tail of a peacock; and a long and half-hard palm, and it should be finely spun at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	The manner of the urine's exit if you take a double thread and tie it at the tip of the cotton or linen, and cut the tip of the thread with the sewing needle; and remove the excess linen and cut the tip of the thread, then anoint the thread with oil or butter and ointment of urine and urine of ox, and seat the patient on the seat, and the bladder and the vessel moistened with oil of olive and wormwood tea; then gently place the thread in the vessel, as it reaches the root of the vessel, then double the vessel towards the belly; then cut the thread before it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient come out of the bladder, and this is done according to this order because either the guide or the patient will turn; then the thread is all through the linen pouch and pouch, and the urine follows the linen, then it is drawn out further, and the urine is made up; and the siringue resumes when the bladder is empty and the patient is alleviated.
des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are scorching or bloody discharges in the bladder, or when an abscess is formed and you see water and medicines distilling, then use all the instrument called "cathoscopy", and it is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it is third-degree (II on one side, I on the other, as you see), then use the cystoscope according to the medicine you have; if it burns well without addition, then you can draw off the mucus, and if you can, then insert the speculum into the mucus; when you see your medicines running in the bladder, put the head of the cystoscope into the mucus, and draw it out at the drawing-out which is at the end; if you draw out the mucus from the cystoscope, and then forcefully push the drawing-out back in, if the mucus enters the bladder now, and comes to the surface, then the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle cystoscope which is used to catoscope the bladder: if that is the case.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or archaut, and the head is higher up; and then take a sheep's bladder and put on the moister that you see clisterizing the bladder, then lay it between the two eyes to form a double boil, and heat the moister over the fire; then cut the chief of the clistere in the verge, then hold your hand on the bladder all the moister coming out, as if the patient feels that the moister has reached the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make the circle, and perforate it roundly around; then pull the strong thread through these punctures, then assemble the circle as one would assemble a dial, and put in what you see of oil and moister and whey, and lay it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand as much as the moister comes to the bladder.
de la piere	From the incision
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division of the ways of incision and extraction of arrows; and we said the difference between the incision as it should be, and those signs, and in what piere one must over in size; and in the vessie, and in the verge; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the incision which is most often in the vessie is in children, and it is a sign that the aigue of the vessie has jumped to its subtility; and it is open harene, and grates the malaides's verge many times, and then enriches; and then the jumps of the enfans are found; and it is the lightest sanation of the enfans until they are IIII years old, and it is grief in viellars, and it is as jones moiene, for those who are between jonesce and viellece; and it is the cure more legiere for those who have big piere, than for those who have small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, if we cover the patient with cloths dipped in cold water, we must cleanse all the insides.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never closes the wound.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the shoulders, stand up, and move him downwards until the wound reaches the top of the bladder, and does not once rise above it; then place his hands between your hands, and his fingers are flat against his thighs if the bladder is completely deflated; then press and touch the wound; if you feel the wound in its entirety, then now cut at the wound.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier. Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the vagina with his hand, and he commands him to extend his left hand with the fingers upwards, and with his right hand to grasp the hairs that are loose in the part where the cut is made; then he pierces the spatule copant, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	1. And they pass between the ribs and the foundation, not in the costal margin of the left side; and there should be three on either side of the incision, and the size should be large enough to cover if it becomes wide due to pressure, and should be narrowed according to the amount of the incision, not too large; by chance, the pressure should be applied if it is at the foundation, so that it does not cause pain in working; and they should check if there is any part with a piece missing or angles, and margins: if they are rough to come out; and if a part is tied, it resembles a girdle, and curves, whose end is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	1. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is not treated promptly, it can lead to a large wound and further injury.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things can happen to the patient: either they die, or urine comes out due to the urethra not being able to close; but you should try as much as possible to draw it out, or to shave it off with a razor, until you have completed your work. When you have finished, use frankincense and aloe and dragon's blood, and extract it, and put on soft cloths soaked in oil and wine, or in rosewater and cold water, to alleviate the soreness; then stitch up the patient at the base of the urethra, and do not leave any loose thread.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you dislocate it, if the joint is well oiled with oil and sage, then the cure of ointment dyefacient and basilic ointment, until it is healthy.

And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the vein, and this retention of urine, which is done in a way that without jumping with the urine: you must cut out the pus, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will cause the vein to burst, and bleed; then cleanse the wound with oil and sage, and all other means you know, until it is healthy; and it is necessary that all the times you treat it, that you lie the thighs and assemble the medicines under the armpit.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the prick is small and it is conducted with a needle, and it is cleaned, and the urine cannot be discharged; if the treatment I described fails repeatedly, you will be excused for the size of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already done that.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Prepare to forge according to this form and make it at a third angle, one ton.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the wire and pull it through the hole opposite the prick, so that it does not get stuck in the vessel; then bend the wire around the needle lightly, as it reaches the prick; and turn the wire back to your hand at the prick as much as you can, until you can feel the prick from the other side; if a lot of urine comes out, then press your hand on the part where the needle is stuck in the hole.

If the bone is so broken, and it breaks with urine, and the gut of the patient; and if you do not know how to do anything else, then cut off the end of the piercing and the other side, then make a groove between the two bones, then pull out the piece that was stuck, and remove the ligature that is in the wound; and treat the patient as soon as they are healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the piercing of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	If the piercing is not enlarged in women, and if there is no time, then the cure is done by three things: one is that by chance the woman is a virgin; the second is that it is not possible to find a woman well knowing who has been defiled as much as she has, even when she is cast.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the third way is if by chance one cannot find a skilled woman in this art of hands; and the fourth way is if the woman's wound is more than the man's, because it requires a more precise size, and great pain it causes. And if necessary, remove her to this, and choose a woman well knowing, and if she does not know, then cast a subtle spell; and she presents a wise lesson in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and commands that she do what you command in the inquisition of the wound; and look well if the woman is virgin: therefore it is her duty to bind or found and seek the wound; and if she binds, if she constrains her duty, and recommends that she bind or with the midwife, and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If the wound is large, if it moves little by little from the entrance of the vagina up to the root of the thigh, until it reaches the bone; then cut at the hole in the bone, at the root of the thigh, where it is most sensitive, and do not move the knife above or below the wound, and make it as small as possible at first; then bind it with a bandage, if you feel the wound so sharp that the wound can bleed, and know that there are many kinds of wounds: this is to know, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and crooked, and those that have veins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you want to know the appearance to know the end.

de hernie carnouse	of hernia cancer
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Sweat is nothing more than an assembly of moisture or white sodium, which is contained in the urine; and it is called "soda," and no time is ever properly in the urine, if one cares that it is another urine; and this is the leather between the white soda that we have said; and there was never any.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this sweat is due to the lack of it coming from the bladder, and it is expanded that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	1. And no time when it comes from striking the bones, and this moisture in many colors: either it is declining to jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or white, and this becomes more; and these are the signs of this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then it is the apothecary's remedy, I poc long if it looks like a toy, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	2. And if it has moisture in its own cloth, then it is the apothecary's remedy with a part of the urine, and because one thinks it is other ointments; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the white facial, then it feels well; therefore, when you see the color of the moisture, sprinkle all over the introitory instrument before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introduction, judge whether it is dependent or independent.

And when we come to perform the operation, if it is possible to make the patient healthy according to what we can do and the completion of his chest; then he lies on his back, with his legs spread wide apart, and places a cloth on his body; then he lifts up his right side, and commands the assistant to lift up his left arm, and extends the gauze between the two fifth ribs and the costal cartilage; then he takes the spatula, and cuts through the costal cartilage of the ribs, from the top to the point where the wound is, and makes it as straight as possible, and removes all the blood; then he pierces the wound with a sharp needle at the large abscess, and extracts all the pus, and then places his fingers, and presses the wound on both sides, so that he does not touch the costal cartilage, but only the wound itself; if the wound is deep, then he should carefully remove it, and if the wound is shallow, then he should stitch it with two needles at once, if he does not stitch it well enough, then the wound will re-open; and if the wound is large, then he should assemble the two ribs on both sides of the costal cartilage, and treat it as the other wounds, until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit. And the victory is achieved in all ways that you can; as long as you are diligent in everything. 2. Keeps the head from touching the foot; and cares that this work is more safe; and keeps away from dislocation of blood, and prevents deformity of the limb, and nothing else makes you contrary, whether amputation or dislocation of blood or another thing, if you cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before.

Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine. des emorroides	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de

Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are in the mouth of the wife, one can feel them, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	1. It is necessary that you put the woman in a cool house, then take off the clothes with nails, and cut her hair at its roots, then dust some medicines restricting blood loss, as bitter as ice and blood of dragon and incense, and similar things; then soak her feet in cold water for an hour, then put them in a cold bath; and if she loses blood and comes out, if I make it stay in a decoction of sumac and extract of crab apples and gallberries and similar things, and then take flour of oats, mix it with honey and vinegar, and apply it to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	If it becomes dislocated, it is bad.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it does not become dislocated, make the patient lie on their back and apply pressure to the shoulder; then take the joint, and the joint in milk of plantain or wine vinegar, and apply it to the shoulder.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the wound is healed, treat the shoulder with ointment until it is healthy; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles the sharp herb I mentioned earlier, if it works as expected; and then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	wounds of the marriage bed
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many forms of abscess come in the marriage, like gangrene and puerperal abscess and herpes and fistulas and abscesses and hemorrhoids and chancroid, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, in this treatment, it is necessary to deal with the furuncle that comes in marriage, which is not an abscess but a bowel; and if you see the symptoms of the abscess, if you look at whether the abscess is red at the beginning of its coming, and plain of chill and fever, and if it becomes red, you should see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	1. Therefore, do not hurry to operate, but make sure the pain is subsided; and then place the patient on the bed, and let them have two pillows or adjust their back and assemble their limbs as they fit the leg; and let their knees be slightly spread, and put their hands on their thighs at the groin, and hold them well with a belt; then move the instrument towards the left side, and afterwards come the form of the maw; and it is necessary that when you see the instrument being applied, you fix the first part to know the fitting of the maw, so that what enters through the instrument does not fit more than it should, and does not cause pain to the patient; and if they are larger, it is necessary to cover the fitting of the maw with cloths, so that the patients do not grieve; and it is necessary to place the handle of the instrument at the end, and to shape the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	When the stitches are opened, and it is made into a soft ball in the hand, if it comes close to the head, apply it to the wound; when the bow is visible, it is necessary to put soft tents in olive oil or vinegar oil in the wound; put the tent for the wound at the end of the arm, and put it on the arm and the puncture point that are clean and soft with warm or cold medicines until it is cured; then the doctor after two days of treatment, as long as it is healthy; and never raise the wound and the arm by cloth and honey, and then with honey or roots of lilies and aristolochum that are cooked; then continue the treatment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	If the wound is treated with hot iron, then you must keep yourself from cooking with it, but we have said in the division how to do it.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Childbirth is first in the dance that the woman knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see her press against the bed, and desire to smell the aroma: therefore, hasten to give birth to the child; then assure yourself that these children are according to the natural figure, and they come from your womb, and the second one with him; and when you see these signs, it is appropriate to gently press on his belly if he comes soonest; for when he descends from his head, if he comes with the second one, and is monied by the superfluities of good cleanliness, and that which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For there is no time when it comes to his feet, and it comes to the heart or head, and the hands, or when it comes to his belly or side, and it is converted by chance in his collarbone, and by other harmful figures; if it is skilled in the dance that it is wise and subtle in these things, and warns against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures so that one can help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out naturally at the time of birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her virtues are weak, then if she is placed on a stool or the women hold her, and if the olive oil or fenugreek is cooked, and then the dance is performed between its two small spatula forms.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And the second line, and press on his nail as much as the moisture that is in it to be corrected; and insert the woman's belly as much as the children descend, and if they do not descend, then it is necessary to close the woman's thigh with fenugreek oil; then it should be inserted and fastened with thread, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if now the children are born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands come out further, then it is necessary to gently touch them with a little thread; and if they do not enter, then the woman should sit on her knees, and lift the feet above; then lower the seat on the ground, and examine the woman to make sure she does not have any swelling; and if the hands cannot be inserted, and the children are dead, then it is necessary to press the hands on the coccyx that is in front, and take out the child, and reset it gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's foot
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes to its feet, if it is able to stand; and then it wobbles a little, until it is steady; then it grasps its feet and extends them a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump as high as the command, and I will make it jump from a height; if it jumps, let God be praised.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, if it wobbles a little, until it is in accordance with the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it becomes lighter.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	When it does not come out as we have described, say if it is very difficult to seize, and oil of sweet almonds, and gum resin, and wax all in mortar; and according to the nature of the woman's breast and relieve this pain, then place it in cold water until it becomes numb; when it becomes numb, take the wire of iron, and insert it, and remove it, and leave it for an hour; then place it in the seat, then stretch and close the mouth and nose, and press on the stomach slightly, as the child now leaps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the child's issue when it is born
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if the woman holds her hands close and close; then she should hold onto its neck with one hand and let the other hand hang down, and she should hold the baby's leg with the other hand; and she should fold her hands close and close; and she should press her hands on her stomach and pull the baby's legs apart as much as possible; and if the child does not jump, then she should hold its head and knees, then she should push her belly forward, and then she should give birth; and the woman should have her hands close; and command the woman to press as much as the baby comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out wide with a hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to have an engineer bring the hand: if it cannot be brought, then I will lift the woman; and go; if she cannot go, then I will make her sit on the bed, and straighten the legs; then relax the muscles that I have mentioned; and if there is no child, then I will make her sit on the seat, and study to bring the hand back; and when the child is born naturally, I will stretch it, and command that it be pulled as much as the child can hold.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the issue of the child from its neck, and have expanded its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	1. It is necessary that the patient's hand tingles, then turn it slightly and lightly; when it is equalized, if it is applied with the natural oily nature of musk and oil, as we have said, then it is commanded to move slightly and slightly; when this is done, if it is held firmly at the seat, it is commanded to press; and this is completed.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	2. In the same manner for all subsequent ones.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	3. When it comes to this manner for all subsequent ones, if the second one covers your nail as long as moisture is present; and if the children can be placed on their face and neck, if the covering causes pain, and they die, then cut off the child's ear, as you have done, and command the woman to press no time: therefore, it should be done lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	From the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Sicknesses that occur with twins are often repeated, and never in the third or fourth month; and this is a strange thing, and not many have heard of it.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are strange, and never live long, and few know of them; I know that they are multiplied, and are destroyed by the poison that they give off, which is like the bow; and they never issue naturally as all do under one, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue reluctantly, as we have said, and it is the subtle dance, and made quickly and lightly what it does; and it is done as it should be for salutation.
de plusors enfans	Of more children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No children are ever formed in the marriage of I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more, up to XV, and they are all formed as a child by the measure of the glowing sap, and cover the entire body because of chance, as it seems; if you follow this according to what is needed.
de l’enfant mort	Of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to open with your hands; if it comes that the woman is in good health, and has no accident or dies; if it comes that the woman is well-hung from her back, and her thighs are inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and the midwife applies the teign of II pars, or she is laid in bed so that the child is not born; then gently anoint the mouth of the woman with oily oils with mustard and fenugreek and linseed oil, then anoint her hands with these oils and mustard; then blow on the mouth of the woman lightly, then take I leu or the bones that are flexible at this time, and if the child is approaching its head, you should take the bones from her elbows or collarbone or mouth or beard or chin or chin-whiskers, and if the child descends through her vagina, you should take the bones from her left hand, and put the bowl between her right hand's little fingers, and blow gently on all your hands, and do not let the bone be in any of these places that we have said, until it is out of the thing seen; and this is the form of the bone:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then, if you find another bone, or the other is not yours, and if the extraction is equal; and then, it should be even by moving from one side to the other, according to your ability, and so hold the bones with your teeth, as in this case:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part breaks off, and some parts of both bones are broken off, and the other parts are left; and if it does not break off at all, then place this bone higher up, and continue until all parts are left.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by extension, then wrap it around as in a drape, until it is completely; then the cope is in the joint of the plant or the knee, and it comes that you do it with the other hand, and the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	1. If the child's head is large and misshapen, or if there is a swelling assembled, then it is necessary to remove the spinal bone between your two hands and cut the swelling and extract the spine; or you will use the instrument called "almidach" which comes with the forces or chaperone after it; and then naturally make the child's head large; and then pull on the bones with the tines, and if it is not broken, as long as the moisture that is or has come out is not broken, and if it cannot pass, then it is held by pieces of the mouth that you have; and if it is enlarged in the belly or displaced in the costez, then it must be removed as much as the moisture allows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is among its flock, if it is the light attraction, and the milk of the mother is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the child is in the belly or the thigh, if it covers that you pull it out by the side with your hand; and when the belly or the thigh, as long as the moisture that is there; and if other bones are broken, and the head is dislocated, then bite your hand with the milk of the mother, and draw it to the mouth of the mother; then take the gullet or both, and pull it out; and if the mouth of the mother is retreated because of the swelling that came, if there is no difficulty, then administer moist and light things; and the administrator pours them in cold water and makes them moist and soft.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is in its costume, and you put it in place equal, then do as we have said in the living child; and if there is no harm, if the part fits, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the child is as we have said in the apoplexy cases that come to the midwife; and if the dislocations occur, if it is treated with heat, and it is misaligned.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I see a woman in whose belly some children had died, then consulted another and was told that it would die, the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time came some abscesses in the flesh, and inflamed as soon as they were opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the cure, and I thought long time, and could not soothe the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I used strong astringents for great attraction, and after some days more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was surprised much, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If you thought that it was bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted the wound, and with my hands I felt bones as long as the woman was in better point; and she saw the woman's long wound in a short time, and it was far from the knee; and I do not remember this chapter because when the master did an strange thing, I thought he would help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the dislocation back to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of pressure, where we close the books; and as the head returns to its place, the shoulders are realigned.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Indeed, the corners should be more subtle and restrictive, and made of flat or rounded wood; and the mouth should be no wider than the head, and the margins of the arms should be equal to a palm and a half, and a little more than a palm on each side; and these adjustments should be made in the mouth of the dislocation for opening when turning the corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	1. Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, can be made from flat or rosewood, depending on the appearance of the nails; and it has two heads, as you see, like a palm of the hand, and they are wide; and when you open the mare, as you see with all the instruments, place the woman's foot on the instrument, the thighs and legs over it, then adjust the two heads together in the mare, and hold the end of the instrument's handle between your fingers; then operate your hand with all the instruments, as you have done with the nails evenly, according to the amount you see open the mouth of the mare, until the horse feels comfortable and ready.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	1. These instruments are all similar in appearance, and when they are examined, the more skilled they become at operating them, and the higher they rise in value according to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	2. If you do not despise the instrument that you have not yet examined, because its needs are not easily satisfied.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	3. When the second child is born, if it is necessary to command the midwife to release the placenta, and then to cut it away from the uterus, and to hold the hands of the mouth and anus; and if it leaps for this reason, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, then if I can, and make an opening or covering, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the patient, such as garlic, rose, anise, chamomile, calamus, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, are cooked or can be made into an infusion over fire; then make a gargle or pertus that can, and the other part in the mouth of the patient, and rub it until the vapors come out of the mouth; then make it gargle, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part is fast.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if she remains after this cure, and is not better, then command the patient to put her left hand in olive oil or musk oil, and then let it go naturally, and want the second part; and when she finds it, press and extend it gently so that the mouth does not hurt from extraction; but it must move lightly to the right and left, and then take it; if it comes out and is not damaged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	1. If the mouth of the mare is dry and wrinkled, as we have said, the cure is to moisten and fumigate the herbs; and if it does not do all that we have said, then keep to what we have said, but whatever is in the mare's mouth, tie it to the woman's wrist, then apply ointment tetrafarmacone; if it becomes sore and is replaced, and returns, but if it causes a bad odor in the stomach and head, and makes the patient sick.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	2. If it comes to burning aromatic herbs, no one has ever seen burning of cress and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is such that it burns the woman with the retention of flowers and the second wind if this is:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a snake, and one places the head subtly in nature, and the wide shoulders under the fire; and it is the fumigations from the charcoal, and the blister as it is burned, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to perceive the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And many children are born who do not perceive the foundation, but they have been scorched a little with some subtle sauce: if it comes to the point that they perceive this sauce at their will, and do not perceive any spasm from it, and keep the bandage that does not touch; then put on a fine cloth in wine and oil, and the care of the ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it does not stay, if you put a catheter in its place and leave it hands free, and it is able to move when the child sees them going into the rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never comes this help for wounds or abscesses; if it is needed to cut it: if you cure it, as we have said of the catheter.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula with great foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodulation, and become thicker as they come from the deeper part, or in the space between the two parts; and if there is one nodulation, it becomes rough and blinched or subtle-browned, and never are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by this that they are caused by egestion or ventosity when the patient egests, and by chance some fall.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that pus comes from the bladder, and from half of the vagina; and they reach to the junction of the coxae, and to the anus.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	If you want to know if the fistula is at the base, and not elsewhere: and it is that you cut your index or base, and insert a small hook of iron or gold in the fistula when it is not kinked.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	If there is kinking, then you insert a small needle or horsehair, as much as you can feel it in your hand; and if you don't feel it, and there is no discharge from the rectum, vomiting, or incontinence, as we have said: sharpen the needle or horsehair; if you are in a hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is present in the bladder or conducted from the urine, if it leaks and cannot be stopped by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is present at the joint of the thigh, if it is tight and causes pain in the knee; if it is because of the wound causing constipation, and there is no medicine that can stop it; and in these fistulas there is no cure except for labor and vanity of those who come to it.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not a new fistula and is not an old one, there is hope for health by being made of iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient has pain between his hands on his back; and he makes his legs bend until they are against his thighs, and they are inclined to his stomach; then a tent is sewn or planted if there is tortuosity, as long as you check or the testicle comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	1. If the patient feels pain at the base, then it is likely that the bone has been broken; and if you discover or feel between your thumb and index finger the talon or the hoof, then you should be careful that it is not a foreign object; if it cannot be healed, then it is likely that it is a break.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	1. It is not always possible to heal all wounds, but this is rare; and if it is a burn, then you should make the cauterization as small as possible according to the size of the fistula, as mentioned earlier; and the bark should be cut in the fistula as it comes out from the bone; and repeat this two or three times, as long as you are sure that these charsets are hard, which resemble a quill; then the cure of softened wounds should be made, as soon as they heal, then the cure of ointment should be applied, squeezed and anointed.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is healthy, so good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not healthy, no other sickness can be healthy; and if he tries to enter, and does not pierce the bone that is either foundation or base, and between your hand and the covering a thick covering of char or chalk, you will see the fistula at this point where the covering ends; if the cope begins at the beginning of the fistula, and goes forward before the tent, and then cauterizes after, as it comes to the end of the tent's head; and it will be delivered from the tent, and will hurt; then the charred ones that seem like a pen of a swallow will be destroyed, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If it does not harm you, and cuts between you and the flesh, whether by fire cauterization or medical boiling.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization, it assembles two things: to know, the surgery of these burned wounds, and the stopping of blood and the removal of moisture; then the care of raw edges in the belly or in the groin, as long as the wound bleeds, and it will be the scars in the belly; then cure the wound of sore gums with dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healthy and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes suddenly from the depths, and it is moved away from the heart, if the wound is deep or shallow, and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the heat, and enter that it is the cloth, or the sack, or the char, if it was only a sign of hope and expectation, by the administration of one of the three ways: or you cauterize as we have said, or you cover it with wax, or if you put it in place and cure as we have said; and do not take too much time in front, that you do not cover the part that holds the depth, and let the excretions pass through the desired channel; then the cure, as we have said; by chance if it becomes healthy, or you remove that covering and mundify it when it is covered with wax, or with another instrument; then mend the char that is in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to prolong the fistula in the part where the depth is defended: if it is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time are fistulas made in this way: and when you reach the fistula with the tent, it is either too tight or too loose at the end of the leather, if you take a tent according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you cut it in two, and thread the tent through all the filth in the fistula as much as it is at the head:
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is persuasive at the edge of the deep fistula, take out the thread from that pertuss, and if you reach the head of the deep fistula, assemble the two ends, and pull them apart, and leave one or both; and keep it once, as long as the threads do not come out of these chars that are between two, and close; then cure the wound as soon as it is sore and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you try in all possible ways that you can, it will not work if it is too tight.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not recommended to make the fistula by tightening too much, and then the treatment, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny thistle from which the fistula is made if it is too large or too small, and on the other hand, because it cannot be compressed, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of the embryos.
