Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	These embryos can be of two kinds: either they are dense and hard like resin, and have small and large grains, and are cut at the base, and have a few or many pieces, and are deficient in the foundation and at the foundation's top; but those that are deficient in this way have little moisture and are cut at the base with a piece of turquoise or a piece of salt, and have the color of corns; and the treatment for those who have made the foundation deficient is that you command the midwife to expel the pieces as soon as they become hard and she sees the fetuses, and if you hurry, and can take them with your nails or keep them in your fingers, then cut at their roots; and if the uncinate cannot hold them by their moisture, then lay them on the flat or on the cloth, or a piece of linen, and then cut them off and powder some hot powders that are in the cauterizing leu; or you cauterize them as is said in the cauterizing chapter, and cure them with other treatments until they are healthy; and if the pieces cannot issue, then clysterize the midwife with clyster mordant and sharp as she washes what is at the foundation, so that it may issue openly; and if the midwife's mouth is not preened, and the fillets are hard at the foundation, then the lighter cure is to preen the midwife's mouth or nails with tenails, and cut off the pieces, and cure them as we have said, until they are healthy, and do not fear the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If it comes to pass that you must cut the seam according to this manner: take one thread, thread it through an awl, and then draw the thread on the other side, and turn the two ends of the other thread around the awl, and if it is wide; and then tighten the thread, then pull the awl, and make the other threads, and do so to all of them, and leave the excess sand in the wound; then put the foundation damp with oil or rosewater, or ointment, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to lie down; then leave it as long as it cools, and when it is cold, if the cure of ointment and other cures are needed, so that it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	When the shoulder joint is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dis
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there are knots in the intestines, and by constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the point of a spatulation or your nail scraping out the pus, which does not allow it to get wet; then treat it as much as it is possible, and if it cannot be scraped, then re-scrape it more forcefully until it is clean, and soak it in hot water; then treat it as it is healthy.
dou fremit	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Antor is a small appearance that must be removed from the chest, and it does not move an inch; and never has the patient felt any pain, and it feels like death's trembling, and comes throughout the entire body, and more hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is if you take a nail of a goose feather, or a feather of a vulture, and place that nail on the pulse, as long as the purple circle encircles the pulse entirely; then turn your hand over all the nail as you cover all around the pulse, and put it in its place, and pluck out the pulse from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, if I make this of a nail of iron or silver according to this form, and it is subtle and thin:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you do not perceive, but hold it with both hands and press it; and if you see, if you cauterize the pulse, as in this chapter of cauterization:
de la forme dou clistere	The form of the fire cautery
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never has a clistery been made of silver or archaut, or of melted gold or iron; and never has one been made of these stitches, both small and large, according to the size they are cut.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, in the treatment of children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the fire clistery is small and large if it is made wide, or the belly is made in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a descent or the belly is lied, as you see, and the head is perceived; and it has one of the costals, and the other; and so the belly or puts the medicines into a vessel of a beast or parchment, and perceives all around the small pertus, and between each pertus I must have a spice, then bow in these pertus I weave the strong thread, then assemble the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is given, if the head is held by the instrument before a strong thread, then clisterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of oak bark, or something similar, then gently prick it; then the physician uses his two hands lightly, as he can, then extracts the plaster, and softens the patient's legs at the wound, and if the medicine seems to help, then it is much better; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, then it improves even more.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you are dislocating due to disease of the abdomen, and the physician is hurrying to help, then it returns as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hematoma is or cyst, whether it is the clitoris also subtle as in a child; and this is the form of a subtle cyst under the skin where the hair is pulled:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division of wounds care; and you will say the cures of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the parts where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the point of the instrument, and the size and depth, or lance, or needle, or spear, or similar things; or they are made according to the parts of the body, as a wound that is made at the neck, or at the shoulder, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the shoulder, for the memory will come to your chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, if it is due to cutting or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hemorrhage: if the head is healthier than the rest of the cranium, so if there is little blood from the wound, and the other part is healthy; and avoid the excess of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not seem healthier, if the meat is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat fat, and puts the wound on, if there is hemorrhage, apply olive oil or vinegar steeped in water only; and if there is no hemorrhage, if it puts on the wound, if it is fresh at all its source, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if it has moved, if it puts on some poultices, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a spearhead and its surroundings, and the lips cannot be assembled by tents, if they can be assembled by stitching, if I say as belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is discovered to be against the bone, and it can, and holds only by a point, like a nail; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in leather, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have true or leather for food, and it does not touch the bone, if the whole body is full, and grows weak, then cure it; and if arteries are in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be relieved by medicines, if you want the artery to stop, and if you loose the thread, if the thread is long; and if it does not profit, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	When these wounds are small and simple, if the cure is light: and it is that you place in this powder that smells like the arse has been moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take a part of incense; burn three parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live chalz, and the fine powder, and apply to the wound, and stretch it as it comes together with all its sinew; and then close it well, and leave it to drip, if it does not swell; for one does not waste the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no time has it been done with just chalz, when one does not have incense or the dragon's blood, but that the arse has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is painful, then immediately do this in it; but use some of these powders: either digested ointments, or dough made from wheat flour and honey, until it bends; then continue with other cures as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, then use fine tweezers to remove it; I will tell you more about this later for major fractures.
de la plaie dou col	of a minor wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes or goes and it is simple, but if there is no difference between the two and the collarbone or the artery is not affected.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the bone, and there is no other remedy than leaving it to itself and not putting anything on it, for it will pull out by itself; and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the bone is cold, and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the colder member; but if the medicine is bitter, like warmth in the face, and mixed with rose oil, and washed with warm water, and other piercings made in this way, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, and the edges are not torn, then the cure as soon as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	When the wounds are clean and the hair is long and full of bristles, if the cut or lower down the leg; and if the artery is closed, and the blood comes out in drops when it should, if it is stopped, and the lobe and the cauterization is done; and if the spine of the neck is closed, or the throat, and the conductor is kept, because the meat goes, if the throat is closed at the neck, and does not touch the neck but is returned according to its natural figure; then the strain is removed, and some parts are left, then the cure of scars is done as soon as it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, if it wants to; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are smoothed out as much as possible, and those that cannot be smoothed out, if left, so that the wound does not become infected and becomes healed and allied to the issue; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is put on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If he has bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then the treatment is as I have described in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or the spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from an arrow or spear, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at the wound to see if the patient has lost much blood: then, if it is mortal, and the wound is fresh all over, then do not delay in putting powder on the wound as soon as possible, and do not leave it without applying more powder until the blood stops flowing, and raise the arm, and apply a compress to the wound; but if there is no powder, then put cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three or four hours, or more, until the spasms stop and the tremors of the chest are not felt; and when you see the bones in proper position, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds with remedies and other remedies, as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot be made healthy, perform surgery on them with sharp instruments that have been prepared; as is necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is a cut with a knife or a thrust, and it is simple, or on the back, if the treatment is done by the person in front; if it is large, use poultice; and if it is small, use powder; and if it is infected, and it pusses, and the pus is drawn out with pieces of bone, if necessary; and if the pus does not come out, let the wound be left to drain, if the extractions are performed; and other wounds on other parts of the body are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	A sudden and severe pain in the stomach.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The pain in the stomach is great and severe, and there are many wounds; the intestines are torn once or twice, and sometimes even more, due to the intestinal insertion. And the abdomen is more swollen, and never less than the small wound that the large ones cause, because we reinsert the intestines again and again; because the intestines swell so much that they feel the pain, if they return more often, and because it causes the other wounds, because the intestines are inserted in the belly as others do. And there are four ways to treat the pain in the stomach: the two common costures come from the costure of the stomach, and the costure of the other wounds and the two other costures that are common to other wounds; and all of them are more appropriate with the costure of the stomach, and I will say one by one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no inflammation in the intestines, and it is not a difficult matter to set, this is one of the two methods: either by the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is compressed due to the friction.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is swollen, treat it in this way: moisten a sponge or a damp cloth only, or soak it in hot water and squeeze out the water, and gently massage the intestine until it becomes less inflamed; never forget to do this repeatedly, and it will become less swollen.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the inflammation departing, if the intestine of the stomach or large intestine and bowels are cooked, it is because this is alleviating the entry of a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small wound in the wound with the instrument, and cover the edges with dressing; and the first cure is to cut off that part, which does not have to be cut for great necessity or not; and this is the strangulation for the incision: if it tears from the abdomen and does not cut, and see this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine springs out, if you put it back according to its natural form in its own place, you will have done well, because this is what is needed.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you are able to make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then raise the chest and hips higher than the abdomen, and thus the wound in the one side will be higher than the other; and it comes to administering what I say about large and messy wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you are able to make the patient lie on their back and raise their legs higher than their chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then raise the chest and hips higher than the abdomen, and thus the wound in the one side will be higher than the other; and it comes to administering what I say about large and messy wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I opened the intestine and it had been there for 24 hours, and the wound was 15 years old, and I treated it and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	The midwife showed them the wound that would rot, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat it with any remedy because I could not find any medicine, nor in the world; and I washed it more than twice a day with honey-water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or, you will tell me the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and thread it through the corner piece as close to the edge as possible; when it has perforated the right side, if the chief or the coast is thicker or thinner than the needle, and you have threaded the needle, make another perforation on the other side of the denuded part; and they understand this sewing if you do it as the tailor does the fur, and leave once the thread on one side, and take it back again until the seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen referred to as his own invention, is the most common and is used when no other method works. It involves aligning the two ends naturally and applying one thread loop to the other, in this manner: insert an awl or thread loop close to the end, and then perceive that one; leave the two thread loops; then turn the awl, and perceive through the part that is closest to the end, as the thread loops; then perceive the other part through the part that is closest to the end, using the other thread loops that are on the other side; and this is the most common method of sewing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	If the patient hears this advice and no one else gives it, they must sew the belly at the eyes, or as many as there are; and they must insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who have their wounds corroded; and when the flesh is rotten in the belly, it is the belly that is more painful than the other wounds.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	They judge the wound by comparing it to other wounds: and if you find the fresh wound all of its own color, and it has not moved, then you should reinsert the intestine and the bowel; then put some poultice of uncooked char on it, and if it has not moved, then put any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is bloody; and cut the thread, and be sure to sew the wound as tightly as possible, and check the stitching; then treat the wound as you would any other, until it is healed; and if you have no medicine, then put some on, as often as it gushes blood, cloth wet with vinegar, and mix it well until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other skill in other positions than the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communiteit as principal members, then it comes that you lightly oint with oil of temperate chalor, or oil of rose, and put on bandages, and remove the stings; and if there is pain or rash in the bellies, and often comes, if the clisterize of red wine German, and also the rash comes to the intestine; and the perce dedens, and saiches that when it is the big intestines, it is lighter to heal than the little.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the veins that surround it, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to the nature of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gash is jumped from the wound, and it is reset as tightly as the intestine while it is fresh; and if it is large and turns black, then you must lie down the black part of the limb that is black, because it has veins and arteries; then deal with what is between the ligament, and pull the heads of the arrows away from the part of the wound until the extraction is pulled out when the gash jumps, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, if it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were wounded or had an opening in their bellies; and this was the wound on the left side of the stomach, and it was infected and became a fistula, and therein was the egestion and the vents; I treated it according to what I could, and did not stop subtleizing until it was healthy, and I examined it.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it sutured, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but he had none, but he delayed better preparations, and did not eat or drink; and they said to no one whoever had a small wound in the intestine, that one must treat it in this way: take large testes, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the mouth has overturned the testicles, if you can pull them with the lips, then close the testicle; and then hold it there as long as it does not slip, and then make another fit in the same way that before, until the wound is entirely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	1. de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula," and also if they are thin and have a narrow opening.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the belief that it is hard and filled with pus, or one feels pain, and is as thin as the tail of an ostrich; and never with a narrow mouth, and sometimes wide; and never small, and sometimes large; and I have seen this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and has no pus, it is only due to one of the eight causes: it is to know, by the small amount of sweat or corselet; or because of its malice; or because it has a hard crust, which does not allow the lips to char; or it has too many boils; or the lesion is porous and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or due to the property of the region being slow digestion, and slow health, and flees by nature; or it has bones or holes: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The following lines are the translation of the given Old French text into English:
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	1. Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	1. No time comes with swelling in the knee joint, and it takes a long time for a large gathering of bows to form; then they are cut and pierced, and in a jump, the bows are scattered, and the wounds that result are as delicate as silk, and do not reach the bone or nerve, and such disease is called "hernia," but if it is very long, it reaches the bone, and then it is called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone through the front, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is cut all at once, and at the same time when it is delicate, like silk; and it does not rot because of corruption.

If the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture and cannot stay in place, it must be reset first.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Gangrene is an abscess that develops in the finger, either from a cut or nail, or by chance in other parts; and when it becomes inflamed, and is not attended to, if the abscess breaks, and spreads and blisters as it reaches the root of the finger, and by chance reaches the whole; and comes to corrosions around the bone, as soon as pain comes, and the head of the toe is large, and the color is changed.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, if you cover all the excess that is made from the finger, then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The cauterization is a great help when the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses on the skin, and it begins to prick, and burn, then you should remove the tip of the nail that points at the skin, and cut it off high, and cope with the remaining part of the nail subtly and lightly, and put on the remnant of the nail with medicines that are ardent and corrosive to heal all; then the cure of wounds as long as it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	2. And if the corrosion is in the bone, if it pierces and turns over, because as much as the bone corrupts and becomes, so long it cannot be healed; and if you see the other corrupting, if you cope with it in the way said before, then the cure as long as it is healthy; and if it is hardened and cut off, and it feels great pain, then you should heal it first; then cope the nail with a sharp knife cutting across, and make sure that the nail does not pierce the skin which is far from the nail, because the patient will feel too much pain; and if it happens, then put something on which soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the dislocated shoulder
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The dislocation that occurs in the hands of some men by chance is quite rare, and by chance it can be doubled, and never once it can be broken, and no one is born in the root of the jointure, or the birth is in any of us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are not born with pain in the shoulder do not move, and those who are dislocated at the shoulder by chance move; the size of the one who is dislocated is lighter, in part: size it is like the root of a wide spatumile.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are dislocated at the root of the joint are difficult to cure: if you hold it tight with a cloth.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the case where the head of the shoulder is dislocated from behind, if you can first cover the joint with a clean cloth, then cover the bone with a suitable cloth, and then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The causes that come are either from birth, or from wounds, or from burns, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you can cover the wound, if it needs to be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two sheets or oiled cloths that do not stick together, or put between two pieces of fine linen as long as the wound is sore, just as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	The patient comes to none of its two with the hand if it is not hot enough, as it should be.
des vils	of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Great wounds are swollen and full of melancholic superfluity, which come to more members of the stronger sex; and more often in the legs of those who go to prayer, work, and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must never administer any purge of colic, and then the proper dose of the basilicon.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is given in two ways: one is to follow the black blood, and to take the vein; and the other way is that you should tie the vein, and take it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	1. The length is as follows: first, the hot knee of great force is raised as high as possible, until the thick part is not subtle, then the leg is tightly wrapped around the cuxe joint of the part below the genital; then, the vein is cut in I, II, or III with a large size, then lift and tray the black blood to your hand, from one joint to the other, as much as the patient can bear without pain; then lie down, and command that it be painted with meat in black; and resume the evacuation and cleaning of the wound as soon as the veins are relieved, and do not hurt the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. The legs of the patient are treated as follows: trim the hair of the affected limb, if it has hair, then place it in warm bath water, and heat the limb until it turns red, and inflame the veins; and if there is no bath, then heat the limb with fire, and then cauterize the vein at the knee or in the ankle area; then apply leather to the wound, and scarify the vein from all sides, as soon as it is touched, until it appears red and black, and if it seems like a bloody cord; then boil the rait (a type of herb) until it is raised with leather, and then apply it to the wound; then scarify the leather along the vein as soon as it appears, and lay it on the healing wound, as you have done before, and then apply another piece of leather or more, if you have them, and lay it on the healing wound, and then tighten it, and apply it to the second tail (wound); then remove the tail from tail, as soon as it is all healed, and then apply the leather; and if you cannot lift or raise the tail, and an iron needle is inserted into the strong double thread, and the tail is laid down, and the needle is pulled out, and the tail is raised, and your hand is turned over and back, as many times as it can be; and keep the tail from catching fire, for if it catches fire, and it cannot be lifted or raised, and causes harm to the patient; and when you have treated the tail, then put a piece of linen cloth with fine hair in wine and oil rose; and cure the wound as soon as it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the visor is contracted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then if you tear it forcefully, but do not cut it, and the eye so that we have mentioned before.

de la voinne civile	of the vein of the arm.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may grow elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the skin that comes from the snake and goes towards the cors serpents, and it is found between the hide and the char.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	When the signs of the beginning of this wound are visible if it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then it changes color, and begins to bleed, and like a root of a plant.
