Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And no time the vein hands rain, and moreover when it opens in the joint of the shoulder or shoulder, and there comes out pus, and which falls; cure the donkeys if we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of verses that are born between leather and skin
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "beef disease", because it often occurs in cattle, and is a small scar that runs between leather and skin, and goes up and down the entire body, and feels well at every joint, until it reaches the skin or the belly, and jumps; and it is caused by the food of some humors, such as snakes, lizards, and ascarides or worms in the belly; and one doubts its maliciousness, because when it goes through the body, it rises to the head, and returns to the oil, by chance enters, and destroys the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and closing, if it cannot be helped when the patient will: if it comes to pass that you read the leg and the bone from a far distance and well closed, then cut and pull out, and put it in the chariot, and do not touch it if it is cauterized by fire as it dies; and the greatest harm it does if it comes to the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or near the oil, if it is drawn aside from it the scarform appears, then cut and pull out, and put it in the chariot; and it is necessary to use the physician's hand of medicines dissolved for the human humors for the poor, and avoid the flesh of enjambed animals as food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from winding
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "worming" in our land, and is a pain that comes in certain members, and spreads from member to member; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a woman patient, and I saw one of my arms, and saw a small worm in the vein of the other arm; and afterwards, I saw it climb up as if it were a snake to the shoulder, faster than anything, as if living silver when it cuts through the flesh; the pain left that arm, and moved to the shoulder, and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; and she told me that she dislocated beyond the other arm, just as I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wished for this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Indeed, I have always wanted to make sure that the pain moves from one part of the body to another, but I do not want it to be like this in women; and I thought that this was because the woman had dry skin, and the veins were exposed, and because of this apparent constraint of the ventosity; and I did not know that it is not true for those who are delicate and have moist skin and recovered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, does it open as we have said, if the limb is stretched and held tightly, and then hold it until the constraint of the ventosity is gone; and cauterize the limb; and if you do not see it at your eyes, if the cure for those who have this constraint is like pungent pills, and pills of serapine, and similar ones.
des saiettes	The term "des saiettes" translates
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The sails are various, depending on their appearances and the wounds of the body or they choke.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of the sails is due to their varying points, sizes, and hairiness, as well as their angles, lengths, and pieces; and those that choke in any member do so in various ways: either in the principal members, such as hair, liver, spleen, lung, stomach, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	If the sail chokes in any member of these parts, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears, it means that you should not remove the extraction of this sail, as death comes later in other positions; and if the sign does not appear to you, and the sail is not causing pain, then the wound should be dressed and cured.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	1. When the sign of a fractured skull appears, when the arrow pierces the bone, and the patient falls to the ground, it is when there is confusion, weakness, and dizziness, and inflammation and pain in the eyes, and throat inflammation, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting; and by chance it does not affect the nose or ears; and by chance it affects the speech and voice; and a sudden fall of the white, moist scarlet wound resembles ploughshares, and so it seems like a horse's snort; and if this sign appears, if you are under treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is still in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it is pushed or pulled is that it feels as if it is sticking out to the side, and it seems empty; and by chance, the shoulder stays still like the leg, and in a short time, dark blood comes, and there is cold and cold sweat, and syncope: then the signs of death appear.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arm that is not moving is that there are no signs of inflammation from the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the face turns pale, and he gasps for air and cries out in pain.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	When the shoulder is dislocated in the covering, if it affects the small ribs; and there is great pain and suffering, and the patient gasps; and all the members of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the dislocated shoulder is the stomach, by chance if it jumps from the wound, nothing indigestible of the meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the dislocated shoulder is the belly, and in a single jump through the small intestine, if there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the dislocated shoulder is in the bladder, and the urine jumps in a single jump and comes out, and the patient feels great pain: fatal wounds.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if the face, neck, shoulder, spine, shoulder blade, back, and muscles, and the limbs appearing similar, are only according to other dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the flesh or artery, and it is not exiting, as I will tell you if I can, because you are making such a face.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I have seen one home a spearhead stuck in the root of the nose: I tried to remove it, and it came out smoothly, without causing any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I have seen a game where an arrowhead was stuck in the grease of the oil, and the arrow was removed, and it could not be reached further than the point towards the face, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, without causing any pain to the ear; the wound healed, and I have never seen any accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there was a arrowhead in the throat of a man, and it was the Arabian arrowhead at the ears: I was the beard, and subtle as I could while I took it out, and it was safe for the man.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I took out an arrowhead from my home, which was either in the beard or the stomach, and I thought I would die; and then after 30 days, if it did not change its position, I cut under the arrowhead, sewed it up, and it came out, and there was no accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you have a home where a arrowhead is stuck in the back or buttocks, and it caused a wound to be formed; and the arrowhead did not come out easily, and did not change its natural positions, and did not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if another man cuts himself on his face, and feels the wound; and does not immediately feel great pain; and does not think of other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was a wound on the face of a prince, the king, who had it cut by a sharp instrument and was swollen on the left side; and it was all puffed up. I was called for the cure after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If you find the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to open it with all my skill, and I did not feel anything; but I felt a sharp and painful sensation in my left ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed the leg on the uneven surface, because the arrow did not fit; and it seemed to me that it was from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the bandage on my hands, and it soothed the right side of the wound, and delayed the patient's pain for a long time until he felt the arrow in his flesh; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied the poultice of the corrosive medicine on my hands, as it was overturned, and I touched it, and I felt the head of the arrow in the flesh; then I turned the overturned part of the wound with that medicine, until the patient's pain seemed to disappear; and it healed well within four months, and then it was removed when the stitches were removed, and I could not do it; therefore, I continued to refine and invent ways to extract, as soon as I put on the needles properly, according to the form that comes at the end of this chapter, as I draw and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The shoulder joint is judged to be unable to heal: I will heal it therefore, and the wound was soothing the pain, and the patient became healthy completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have said the quality of extracting some arrows, so you should apply your cure according to what I do not say, for the books cannot make everything appear dirty; but the masters of the arts know how to use well chosen things and the present and deficient ones, true veins, and sharp instruments, in descending from the things strained which come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not come from the limbs or they are falsely stuck for according to two ways: either by the hand or they enter, or by another part; and the one that is thrown from the hand or it enters, it is an arrow that enters into the joints, and it has never been thrown once.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	If she does not jump now, if the horse is not overheated and the jaws are not closed, then she will become unconscious and remain so until another joint is opened; and thus, she falls into the bone, and she cannot move if there are no other joints, and each joint; and therefore, she falls, and she does not fall if a subtle cut is made at the end of all the parts that are open, as long as the jaws are not closed, and then the tail.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the chest, and it goes into one of the lungs, or any other accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: if he does not pull it out immediately, but leaves it as long as it remains calm after a joint, then the patient will die.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the dislocation is not caused by the bone alone, and does not cause any other injuries, and the patient has had no previous accidents, then the surgeon should intervene.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is not caused by the bone alone, and cannot be corrected, then the surgeon should immediately call for assistance; as I have told you. Then, treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the dislocation is not visible in the limb, and one cannot see it, and the patient wishes to try everything; and if you feel it, if there is no instrument available to reduce it; and if you do not have any force or skill to reduce it, because the wound is large and the limb is painful, and the limb remains painful even after the wound has healed, then reduce the dislocation as much as possible, and if the limb has ears that hold them, then use the bone that is causing the dislocation as a lever, and then break or crush the ears of the limb, until you can reduce it; and do it very gently, even though you may have broken the limb.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it once, if the bone is still wet until it is read, then pull it out, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the dislocation does not move in the direction of the bone we have said in this chapter; and you are given an incision on the nerve and the vein, and you insert a needle as you please to draw out the arrow, whether it is quickly or slowly, or firmly or loosely; and you put the bandage according to the shape of the wound that the arrow made, because it is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not, if you do not follow what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The patient feels pain in the shoulder, either from another cause or because the skin is too tight in that place, so it should be cut: as soon as the stitches can hold, it should be pulled out: if there is no further pain now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If the bone is held in place, if the hand turns around as it enters the bone, until it expands the bone, then it should be pulled out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be extracted, leave it alone and continue the extraction as soon as it starts; if the arrow is in the wound, if it comes out of the wound, and if you see blood, if the point of the arrow enters the instrument's hair, then pull out the arrow and the instrument's point that enters the wound, to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrowhead is lodged, then you must remove the entire shaft or the venom if it is still inside. Then, treat the wound as best as you can.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrowhead is lodged in the chest, abdomen, or intestines, and it is protruding, then you must remove it. If it is still inside, then pull it out slowly, and then cut the vein and nerve, and then extract the arrowhead. Then, treat the wound as best as you can until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the arrowhead's points used to treat wounds is similar to the beak of an owl, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are different ways of doing it: large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed hair is similar to that of an owl's beak, by inserting it at the tip of the arrowhead, as shown in this figure:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tines for insertion and removal is similar to this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	of which the veins are common, and of which there are XXXI, of which XVI are the largest, that is to say: the two branches that are after the ears, which are called the "herbage" arteries; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and the veins that are in the two cheekbones, which are called the "aspirations"; and the vein that is cut in the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the guinea worms which are at the neck; and the veins that are in the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the veins that are on the underside of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The first line of the text translates to: "The veins commonly found in each arm are V: one is the cranial, and is on the left side of the costal, and is called the 'grievous man's vein'; and the other is called the 'fast' vein, and is composed of the cranial and the basilar, and is called the 'grievous man's thoracic'; and the basilar is on the left side of the costal, and is called the 'grievous man's abdominal', and is located under the scapula, and is the one that is found in the arm, which is open manifestly under the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The savable part is the vein that is between the auricle and the anus, and if it rains; and in the leg and where the patellar tendon is, there are three veins: one is the coronet of the medial condyle of the femur, and the second one is called "sesamoid" that is in the medial tibial tuberosity; and the third one is the "nasse" which is in the lateral tibial tuberosity; and in the other leg, there are three veins similar to those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The salvation of the veins after the ears if aids in catheterization and migration; and the quality of the sainment, as I said, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and wipe the leu or the veins with a rough cloth; then the patient's face becomes stringy at the neck, until the veins appear between the ears in the two eyes depending on the head; then give the lancet, and cut through the vein jointly with the bone, then gently hold the hand over all the veins until you cope with the skin and the veins well, and make the incision as much as you can see; then you pull it and hold it until it is healed, and I have already said the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	1. The health of the two arteries located in the temples, if they are prone to migraines and pain, and habitual, and if the quality is such that I say: and it is that the patient draws in his collar as much as the veins open widely; and one feels the looseness of the skin on both sides, and then swells; then gently lift the key above the vein at your index finger, and cut the lancet, and gently raise the vein and the wound, as you have done in the other veins, and make sure to draw out the necessary amount of blood according to your need; then release the patient, and put your index finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then let it form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their comfort and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The patient with the vein in front is as sick as the one with the cranial head, suffering from ancient face diseases, migraines, and bruising. If the physician finds that the patient's head is pulled back by twisting it, as the vein becomes visible; then take the instrument called "forceps," which looks like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and firmly hold it with your hand or another thing, and let the blood ooze out according to the quantity you see; then cut off the hair from the neck, and tie the vein as soon as it is safe and never once with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Every part, it only needs the flame to be too big; and the right way, because the bone is near, and by chance the flame breaks when it is being subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the two arms if it helps them, and the shoulder, and the wound, and the orifice in the oil, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their health if it is that the physician pulls his neck twisting any ligament, as before; then the right way, and so the healthy one, a small part long and wide flame, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the flames are subtle, by chance they are very sharp; then make a deep cut, as much as you can manage, and then tie the cloth, and hold it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	If the wound is not deep and does not cause much pain, but is more like a scrape, and it is on the face, and there is redness and heat that comes with it, and it becomes more noticeable as it gets older; and if the cleanliness of the wound is not good, then strain the wound with your left hand, and take a subtle flame and touch it to the eyebrow that is between the two eyes, because the wound does not open well, and it will start to heal now; do not apply too much pressure, and make a deep cut according to your needs, then tie it for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	1. If the patient has two children, it helps in the relief of labor, at the beginning of childbirth, and for various diseases, such as epilepsy, corrosion, and herpes, and warts; and if the quality of the patient is that the midwife tightly grabs the collar of one and the other, as we have said; and if the midwife is standing at the head of the woman, and the woman is sitting on the bed, then cleanse the vein of one long and widely, then drain the blood abundantly, as much as possible; then do another part in the other vein, then loosen the line, and tighten the veins gently so that the midwife does not strain; and leave it until the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the lips of the deer if they help to close in the mouth, and corruption of the genitals, and cracks of the lips, and sores and throat.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health if it is to make the patient stand before you, and pull his collar as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the eyes, of which one is on the left side and the other on the right, and they are black because of their dark color and the thin dark hair: therefore, cut each one, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest of each part, and do the same for all the eyes that are swollen and closed, because it is a different way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Of the health of the tongue if it is red after the health of the head, and it is at the gorging of the throat, and diseases of the eyes, and diseases of the mouth; and it is healthier when the patient has washed his hands before the sun, and he has cooled the tongue, and looks into each corner of a black vein: healthy therefore one and the other, and do not alarmed too much, for these are arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The red veins that are usually healthy are red in two ways: either by pressing on all the fire with a wide flame, or by olive oil that is as fine as the trenching, and they are called "anesil"; and they are wide and fine according to the width and gorging of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the burned face is such that it is not named, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has the skill to open the flat veins of large blood vessels that contain large blood and cause problems; and this is the form of the burned orange face.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtle applied, and it is safer for the subtle veins, or if there is subtle citrin sang in them.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The salve of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are full of the throat, and the collar, and the stomach, and the belly; and it is necessary for the healer to make wise use of it, and to avoid the artery that is full.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If the artery is pricked and blood comes out, if it can be stopped, then it should not be pricked more than necessary, but cut if possible.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basin does not open clearly, if you pull it, and change to another one; or you do not want any rain on it, or you want to draw the vein from the arm: it opens clearly; and the flame is lit at the basin, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the vein of the patient flowing clearly, if you continue to pull the arm, until you touch the vein as much as possible; then sign the vein is full, and then release the arm, and cut the vein with the flame at the basin; and be careful not to hurt the artery when you see the vein swelling, because it is the artery: close the basin.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you see something emerging from the top as if it were a child's urine, and it is red and subtle, and it looks like it's not from an artery: then hurry, and put your hand far away, then press on the spot where it is not moving, many times; hold the shoulder, let go, and do not move the patient's arm; and be careful, and do not move it until it is safe.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not inflamed, and it is painful, and the doctor is not present, then open the artery if it seems to be open, because the head of the needle has retreated; and inflate it.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a scalpel from the fistula, and cut it, and take one of the halves and sew it well to the other; if it is not stained, that is good; but if not, then the cure, as we have said, with the powders that stain blood; and the stains are not more in other positions for the small wound of the wound, and the pain of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The health of the vein is in harmony when it treats the wound with blood from the head and chest, as we have said; and it is necessary for the physician to treat the nerve that is injured, and if it does not become too much, and it heals the nerve, and it becomes soft and healthy, and by chance cannot be healed; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open any holes for its subtlety, then it is necessary to cleanse the wound with the instrument; and remove the nerve from your body.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is blood flowing between the two veins, if it is long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The treatment of the head if it helps, that it attracts blood from the head, and helps the eyes; and it is the best to touch with olive oil or warm iron, because it is the most safe of all wounds, because it does not harm the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Indeed, it is best to make the bone lighter, and do not hurt anything the first time, and continue; and by chance, the bone may be found in some people, but it does not hurt anything the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your perception.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about health is that it is not acquired overnight but must be maintained for good health and to avoid diseases coming. It can be achieved in one of the three veins: head, fast, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of a patient's first dose, and again after a few hours or the next day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The health that is maintained with diseases has no specific determination, but it depends on the amount of time spent in bed or nursing, in all hours and ten times; and it is not necessary to maintain good health for children until they are fourteen years old, and women until they are four months pregnant.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Necessity does not apply to those who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If the stomach becomes ill due to eating light foods, and if there is a tendency for the intestines to become inflamed, even if there are no excessive amounts of meat or wine, and if one does not have a history of colic or vomiting, and if the belly is distended and the woman's parts are multiplied, and if one does not have too much virtue, or from the arms or from traveling and waking and dining, and if one has the strength to endure all of this, then one should subdue the humors by eating foods and drinks and medicines, as I have said; then take a bath, and nothing will harm you, except for subduing the blood, and to become healthy from the inside out, and then work and rest and luxury and such things, and be loyal and loving, and be healthier than those who are sick, and rub your arms two or three times, and then draw them away gently, because if they are too cold or dry, you cannot bear it without; then rub your hands with a little oil, and then put your left hand on the part of the belly that is sore, and apply a little ointment made from fat to the wound, so that the belly does not become infected when it heals.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like cords to the healer, and if they are too many, as if they were made of wind, then when one puts on fire, it retreats from the fire, and cannot open the vein, and then it is one of these; and if it opens the vein, then it is the wound too tight, for then it comes to advise the healer in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, then it continues a little more of that joint or soon after, and if it is not bent, it is not bent.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the patient is short-sighted and the member swells, and it is left alone for one or two days, and does not tie the arm: by chance, pus comes out; do not bathe, then resume the cure if it pleases; and if the fissure is small, or the member is not cut subtly and you doubt that there is as much pus as you see, since it is so small in the fissure that the patient thinks it is not injured at all; and the wound heals quickly, otherwise, if the fissure is large.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the member swells and if you do not resume the cure with a little oil, since it softens the skin of the pus and makes it worse in this fissure that the oil lies on; and then apply oil to each wound that you cleanse the veins, to stop the course of the pus; and this itself causes triage and bowels to empty when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If large abscesses appear, which come many times, and if it is not healthy to open the vein even once, or if the opening of the vein is small, then soak a soft sponge in cold water and wring it out, and stretch it for an hour; and it is necessary to do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if there is no black or greenish discharge at the site after several days, then you should not know it; and if you see, put nothing on aloe or mirrory jelly in water, mustard, or any similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is gangrene and appearance of the health of the basilica: then place your hand on it, and if the limb is cold to the touch of your hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not place anything on it that we have said, for by accident in the operation without cutting the artery; but I apply it dry to strengthen the limb, then another treatment, until it is healthy.

des sainies de ventouse	Of childbirth pains
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of iron, or of bone; and ventosation is performed in two ways: either by cutting and pulling out blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventosation which is made by cutting is done in two ways: either it is all on fire, or on fire; and ventosation which is made by cutting and extracting blood is made in twelve degrees of the chest, of which one is the chief; and the others are in the col; and the others in the costeis of the col; and the ventosation of the chin; and the ventosation of the shoulder; and the ventosation of the elbows; and the ventosation of the knees; and the ventosations of the ankles; and ventosation does not touch any veins, for only small veins that are scattered in the chest, and therefore no one can suffer from it like a sickness of the veins; and it is only necessary that it be maintained, neither on fire nor on any fire, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as the chest is dry.
