The wounds that are made to hurt are those that are made above the liver, and above the spleen, and the foot, and the belly, and the bowels, and the gall, because this member does not suffer much pain outside of the body, and only feels it when it is attracted by the sanguine member to the other; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we do with vomiting on the belly and the bowels to alleviate the member; and to relieve the pain when it has opillation or piercing, if it is attracted by its own virtue to the opillation, or if it leaves the piercing of its loins; and then it is made according to what is put in the liver and the spleen when it has retained ventositeit, and these vomitings are administered empty to suck only; and they are never administered together with fire, and never with aqueduct tede, as in diseases that cause pain in the pleuresin, and in such a way that one fills the vomiting with hot water, or with what has been cooked herbs, according to what.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum device administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two palm-wide halves of parchment, and has a small pertus on either side of the first petit, as if to poke an needle, and is of iron, with a point facing forward so that it does not scratch the patient's shoulder when inserting it into the member; and in the middle has a groove of iron or steel for a threader to be held, and there are large and small ones according to the disease and the age of those who take them, because the vacuum devices of children are different from vials, and thin than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	The text translates to: "And it must be placed on the wound in the member: take the lead or liniment, and insert it through the vertex of the wound that has been made, so that the lead does not burn the patient; then place it on the member, and you must place it on the pulse points that we have mentioned, if you see, if there is vapor coming out, and you will remove the lead; and take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the wound where it is administered to a patient with pneumonia, all the verges and pulse points are absent, and it is not in a state of fever until the patient becomes feverish, and it is placed on the member only at that time; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	1. Withouts are not removed except in parts where one can put a glove, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in these parts, if they are swollen like char, such as dogs or cats, and other similar parts. And if the quality of the user is that when you find swollen parts that are in soft waters, take them and put them in a gentle water, as long as they are not pregnant, and have nothing in their bellies; then it is healthy for the vein and the wound, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the withouts; and when they are flat and smooth, if it is the hand or one can put a glove, put it on, because it is after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift the leg of ease, and then the stiff one; and if you find it too late after the corset of the loose ones, then dip your hand in cold water, and put on as many as the loose ones are tightened; and if the loose ones multiply, then put on vitrol or gas, or similar things, until they are tightened; or you can cut the leg of half-burned legs and leave them as they burn to the leg, if it now sticks; and if you have more of these, then take more loose ones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the loose ones do not take hold, then wet the leg of sacred water, or take a needle and thread it as much as it needs, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the sacred water, if they burn; and when you see that they are cherishing, then powder some aloe and silk or charcoal, or smoke, if they now cherish.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it treats of wounds and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Therefore, I advise you, dear reader, that you should not believe that this chapter contains nothing new, as you will not find anything in the ancient books, nor any letters; and for this reason, science has been neglected in our country, because I have found no one who knows it; and I do not know anyone who has studied it, except through the science of the ancient books, or by experiment, and by habit in my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the stumps that are amputated, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say this is the introduction of this book, the words and chapters, and the patient understands them, and learns the truth, if those who have experienced it can teach and learn this noble art, and teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that if there is any fracture, dislocation, twisting, or tightening, and nothing else helps, if it is not too weak, nor too faint; and if you hold it is not very tight, nor too loose; and if the hands are cold, it is to know that cold joules, and char of hare and deer, and do not drink wine, nor eat few lean chars, and do not fill the veins with blood too much, until you have no doubt of apoplexy chaut, nor expansion of matter in the member; if it swells again under the same government as it has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the meat that causes great swelling, or if there is viscosity, like wheat cooked in hot water, and tests, and pies, and pancakes made of wool, and cheese, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the swelling that is recovered, the fracture gets worse and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that the bones broken and cracked cannot be well recovered or stitched according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, and those who are too soft; but if it is not cured, first reset the large tendons that were torn and joined with the member, as much as before; and do not wait for a long time, and for this reason it is necessary to stop eating large amounts of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	The treatises of the physicians declare that there are many ways to break bones.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the arm or leg, and I will tell you all the ways of fracturing in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that occurs when falling, and another when struck, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, and a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own way and instrument for restoration, according to what remembrance comes to the patient's mind; and it is the fracture of the bone that is caused by the bone being twisted and widely opened, and pressed with the hand; and if it is not twisted or the mallet does not feel much pain, there is no fracture, but it may have a twist, a fissure, or a small crack.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only move it with your hand, but put the medicine that comes after, and then pull it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should check the fracture that will occur in the bone, and the two parts that are separated, they should be adjusted now, unless the wound is bleeding; and if the wound is bleeding, then it should not leave any part, as long as the wound is calmed; then it should be placed evenly and gently in the hole that you can hold lightly and wisely, and you should check that the restoration of the bone is lighter than the restorations of other bones or if they have pieces; then the extraction, if it comes after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	When there are broken pieces in the bone of the foot, if they are two parts, it is hands or fingers, or a part of your hand that is some small members, or two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are aligned, if you adjust with your fingers the additions in their place in the muscle that you push, and keep that there is no pain or injury to the patient's bone; and straighten well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels good in your hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully and is not strained too much, do not press as much as those who come by their own experience, such as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the member is at its end, if the patient well controls the helper that it does not move, neither by watching nor sleeping nor turning, nor in any other way; and be well that the member is firmly held so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it does not feel any pain, if it is not at its end, and it is necessary to put the member in order so that it does not feel any pain; and keep it straight so that twisting does not come until it is restored; and the quality of the broken member is according to what I say.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	I advise that the broken member is various in smallness and in size and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For if it has eaten members, like bread and butter and similar: if it comes with rolled-up linen cloths and subtle things; and those that are large, like a large bandage and thick rope: if it comes with a wide and hard rope, for the large bands tightly encircle all the great member, and draw it evenly, unless it has no joint; then it is lightly bound with loose knots, three or four times around the member, and the hand is tightly tied once for each part of the member, then go to the end of the fracture and draw it less, so that the fracture is slightly moved a little part of the healthy part, then take another bandage, and turn the other end towards the broken part; then return to the part opposite the fracture, and draw it gently, not too tightly or too loosely, as we have said in the first part of the fracture; then place the rolled-up linen cloths or ribbons between the bandages as they are even, and then tie everything with a bend, and if it has not swelled or inflamed,
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it is infected or gangrenous, if one applies something soothing to the gangrene, which alleviates the infection and leaves no marks; then one should press on the wound, and it should be of half a wide, well-cured cainne (cane), or of fust (dried bark), or of rains (raiments) of palm, and it should be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	However, it is necessary that the thing that is put on the wound be larger and broader than the others; and it should also be as long as it is needed for the member of small or large size; then press on the wound as you did in the first place, then tie a thread around it as you did in the first place, until it is tighter; the further it goes, the less; and the thread must be clean, not too thick nor too thin, and be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, like the works of the fools who make their lingers of linen threads, it is a great error, because the wound cannot be as tight as it should be if it is too fine, and it only serves to have less space between each stitch.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the sharp edges of the stones after being washed with water, if they are not covered with linen or cloth, so that they do not freeze.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the tweezers, and the hair is broken, I will tell you the treatment for this after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should not try to pull out all the broken bones at once, as it is dangerous.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not recommended to put stones in them immediately, after 4 or 7 days, or according to your strength; and as was done by the ancient surgeons to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting: and that you take flour that is between the husks of the mill, and knead it with a lot of water, and make this dough, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way to restore fractures in other positions, as well as for women and small children, because it is not too hard or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend fractures and dislocations and twists: take barley, linen, gum arabic, and Arabian rubber, in the ratio of 20 parts; mercury and aloes, in the ratio of 5 parts; alechil, in the ratio of 18 parts; and grind them into a powder, mix with honey of soap; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster as it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to treat twists: take Arabian rubber and muguet, in the ratio of 20 parts; mercury and aloes, in the ratio of 5 parts; acacia, in the ratio of 6 parts; arsenic ointment, in the ratio of 1 part; mix well, and cook with water or honey of soap, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to mark joints and bones are their levers, and soothe the pain that follows, and the strength of the bone: take new linen, and the oil and lard cooked, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore flesh, but it is necessary to soothe the post-surgical pain and the true bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make plasters that repair broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and earth oak leaves, and crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make plasters for the repair of bone fractures and to help with the recovery of post-surgical pain.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	1. Take the root of mugwort, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of wheat, and each part; and grind them, and mix with wine, and apply to your skin, and rinse with fresh coriander water or with any other water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	2. Another way to apply it more frequently than the first, when the wound is firm, comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	3. Take the roots of mugwort, and linseed meal, bay leaves, honey beeswax, and violet and chamomile flowers, each part; grind them, and mix with salted or sweet water, or wine, according to the health of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that it is not recommended to apply anything on the broken bone to restore its strength, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too wet nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen suggests that on the broken bone to restore, one should apply things like dry and warm substances such as mustard and aloe, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to relieve the wound and pain: take some ointment and powder from the tails of rabbits or the feathers of geese, and vismallow, and seal it well, and the limbs, and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain in his joints or bones; if it does not happen by hand pressure, and pain comes to the joint or prickling, or swelling, if you hasten, and release it, and now the plaster is applied; take a light damp cloth, a sea sponge, dip in cold water, and immerse in cold water, and raise the limb until the prickling stops, and soothe the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, smooth with cold or rose oil, and put on a bandage as soon as you are sure of no aphasia, and let the inflammation in the member subside, and soothe the pain, then resume gentle massage and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much; gently until it is healthy again.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the wound is gushed with blood and there is pain and swelling, and it is inflamed all over, and you have skill in plastering and bandaging, if it recurs, as you did at first properly.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if you see that the wound does not bleed as we have said, if it does not ooze for more than three or four or seven days; and never more than twenty days, as we can see, until the break is healed and approaches the bone; then the restraint should be greater than before, and the tissue should enlarge, as I have said before; and if you see the wound becoming drier than it should, do not let anyone touch it, but instead apply hot poultices every time you deslime it, and every day, and place a piece of cloth over the member; through this means, you can cut out the pus from the wound, and stop the pain that the flesh causes: this is harmful, and if it does not improve, and I see no other way than to cause more suffering and to do it more correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various kinds of wounds
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are various kinds of wounds, and different shapes, and the causes are assigned; for there are wounds made by the thrust of a spear, and the bone is cut all the way through the bone, as if it were a knife or a blade; and therefore this kind of wound is called "cut" or "stab.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spear strikes the bone through different senses, and this kind of wound is called "absolute" cut; and these are the wounds of those two great or small gashes.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a thrust embedded, or cut, or from the bone after the piercing, or from the other side of the piercing, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent fracture, which draws the skin that is loose from the bone, or it is under the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If the wound is healed in the bone as well as under it, and is a small cut, and for this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound is made by injury, or by piercing, or by seeming thing, and lets enter the piece of the bone, and is the same size as when they entered the heating irons; if it enters through the pierce.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more cases than those with dry bones, just like that of a child; and they occur in all these ways of fracture that are lightly broken, just like these; and I will speak about this in their language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us consider all ways of fractures by the methods used for them, and by the corrupt char that is used.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one has discovered the bone, and froths with their hand, if the dark fracture is open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, keep in mind as many accidents as possible of the midwife, and if you see no such accident, then like vomiting of cold, admission of understanding, extension, flexion, congestion, fever, and the wounds turning red and swelling, and other symptoms in various dispositions, if it cannot be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the first pain comes to you, and it is in the shoulder, then it is necessary to stop the movement of the bone before the fourth month at the muse.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If this is the case, and you stop the movement of the bone before the ninth month, then the tendon of the bone will be corrupted, and the accident we have mentioned will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the fracture of the bone comes just before the tendon, and it is necessary to cut the part that is broken, then it should be cut in all the ways you can: the head of the chief of the mutilated patient, and the figure of the wound more than you can imagine, and if the blood comes out to reveal the bone, or if an apothem is caused, then help what is necessary, and if the wound is oiled with soft oils, and the plague is calmed and secured, then the plague should be stopped, and the bone should start moving again, and it is done according to twelve ways of mutilation: one way is when you cut at the end that is narrow, and it is in this form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then, cut another piece of the same size as the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and made of iron; and you can shape them lightly without damaging the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and brittle, then it must be perforated through, otherwise, you must sharpen the edges with files, and do not make them too pointed so they do not pierce the bone further; and you should have more files, so that each time it fits in the bone socket according to the bone's shape; and this is the form of the three methods of files:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	1. The quality to perceive the broken bone is that you place your thumb on the bone, and turn it until you feel the bone is perceived; then put your thumb back another part later, and then do everything around it, then cut the incisions in the bone that is between the points, and do it as gently as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as you draw the bone with your hand, or with any of the instruments that we have like needles, tweezers; and keep from touching the brain or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and cut the bone, if the wound covers the other instrument that seems like an incision, but it should be thinner and more gentle than the other incision; and if there are no small bones or scales, if the light bones are gently on the instruments; then cure the wound with tents and needles that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to open is if it is like the Galenic method, which is more correct; and the larger incision, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the open fracture is visible, so that when you have removed this part, if you measure from the top of this incision, the form is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part is turned towards the bone; then make a small incision, if you lightly cover the entire bone, and take good care of the cloth that is loose; if it is near the bone, if the bone is lightly touched, because it is sensitive to injury, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	When the bone fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only crushed by itself, and it has small pieces, if they cover the rough edges, and smooth the scales with a subtle rasping tool that you must have various quantities of, to adjust each joint according to the degree and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave in front of a coarse rasping tool, and then use a more subtle one, and continue doing this as much as it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In all other hair removal and subtle fracture treatments, it is necessary to adjust according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be reversed for the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	When the scar is discovered, if it comes to pass that you pregnant the wound with linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and the ointment in rose oil, and put it on the wound; then take another doubled bandage of II or III, and the ointment in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first bandage; and do this more gently than you please, so that you do not burn the scar, then apply other linen, and do not strain it as much as it pains the wound only; and leave it for I day or II, until the inflammation is appeased, then remove it, and apply medicines as follows: roots of lis, flour of times, powder of incense, aristolochine, and similar things; and make powder from these things and put on the wound, and apply further medicines without sutures; and wait that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave on it the ointment, or assemble bowels, for if bowels are assembled on the bare skin, they will cause great harm to the patient; for if one puts something mouthing on the wound, it causes great pain to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Preparation is necessary, as no accidents come to the patient if we follow what we have said, if it is doubtful, then there is doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no harm comes from the medicine we have put on it, which has its virtue, then you should apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and a drop of glue, and then cover it with a drapel; then cure it in ways that are suitable for the wound, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Scars that have never been broken are the two parts of the bone that were not cut, or only one, because they are two bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off your small finger or toe, and make the break as even as possible on your index finger, and in the pouch as long as it follows its natural shape; and do this lightly, and let the patient feel no pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the part of the toe that is not the big toe, and it cannot be brought to the heel, then you should put it as even as possible at the end of a thick finger.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in the second part, then you should repeat the first step, and if you can restore the first joint, do so; if not, after the ninth or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then cut off the toe at the end of a thin finger, if the break is in a part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	1. If you cut at another part, it will be; and let the wounds be as large as they fill the cavities.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	2. And no restorer would say that one must soothe the wounds with butter, and each one will die.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	3. It seems to me that it is well, but the wounds must be smoothed with a confection of ouef and molin powder; then leave the wound, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage is firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	4. And never cut on the neck of the wounds, and if it is the first time you have a hard wound, and it holds the breast, and smoothes the pain with a whisper; or as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms at the site while you are working, and it comes to the point where you put on a cloth or cotton cloth greased with rose oil, or in a small vial of laver.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not come, then put on ointment made from flour of bread and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put on light sponges, and do not seal the wound; and if the wound in the nose is small, and it is broken into small pieces, if the pieces are able to be sewn together, then sew them up, and treat the scar with poultices and ointments, as plasters and ointments are able to be used for this; and if there is no wound on the nose, then treat it with compresses and put on needles, as long as it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not deep, but only slightly so, and it is not broken into pieces, but rather bent slightly, which can be corrected with a slight effort.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, to place your index finger in the patient's mouth of the surgeon; and if the fracture is on the left side, then place your index finger on the left hand, lightly press the fracture, and fix it with the other hand, and hold it steady.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	If the fracture of the lower jaw is described as Level II, and you intend to provide extension to the second part, as long as it is equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If the teeth are moving or fracturing, and they are caused by a gold, silver, or silk thread, then take the broken lower jawbone and place it on the ceratoma, and place one double cloth roll; and place the double cloth roll on the upper part of the jawbone, according to its size and width, and tie it with the string you have, and instruct the patient to rest, and give light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, and then return to the same point where it was; and apply plaster with a lot of flour or wheat flour, after you have osteit the ceratoma; and apply a lighter plaster on it, and when it sets, do not change the position of the patient, as long as he is healthy; often it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the wound is infected, then it comes to the attention of the physician, as we have often said.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, it rewards a small piece of the bone in the head; if the bones are slightly crooked, they can be straightened.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is wide, it should be stretched according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all these pieces of bone, and there is none in vain, if the wound is wide, and it is large, and you put on flexible dressings, for mending it as much as possible, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks multiple times in front, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and severed in two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter one to restore; or it is a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the incision is when the break is sensation of wound, that you have two assistants, if the one marks the forceful break; and the other extends your col towards the part; then place the cut equally in your two, so that it forms as it should, and has no appearance or change.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you are skilled at extending, then place the shoulder of the patient against the assistant's shoulder with a round or flat piece of cloth or linen, and it should be large according to your need; and hold and gently apply force, and draw the sphere towards your hand so that you can place the cut equally, as it should be.
