de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm.
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "femur" and one is smaller, and that one is the pocket; and the other is larger, and that one is the opposite side of the small one; by chance, only the large femur or the small one is broken, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the teeth are broken, the restorations are light, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, it is the healing that is poor, and more painful than when they are broken individually.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small teeth that are broken, then it will be sufficient to extend lightly and put even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large teeth that are broken, then they must be drawn more tightly; and extend along the gums, and raise the thumb of the hand higher than the others, and the teeth should be lowered below their own level, and the gums in front of them higher than the labor they suffer; then extend the bones of the arm to the opposite part of the shoulder, or to the other side, and some other bones to the other side.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he places the bone in its place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is in pieces, then he puts each piece in its place, and if there are no loose ends that point to the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then as we have said before, set the bone and the fracture.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if it is with the fracture of a wound, I have spoken to the single physician; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of restoration, apostemes chaus arise, if the thread made of oil of rose and wax is not too hard or too soft, and it is gently draped until the apostemes chaus are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the cervical, and he puts the plaster with a lot of powder from the mill, because he puts the pins, and it is the pin of the bracelet that is larger than the others; and you measure that it must have six pins or arms in more positions: either that the bracelet is in one of the bones, either in two; and it is drawn more under the bracelet than other parts, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and the threads that are under the bracelet wet and moist, and not too hard or rough; and the string, which is drawn out, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some years.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, if you wash the member with hot water until the itching is calmed, and let the member rest for a while.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the stretching, and if the limbs are softened and the bones are exposed, and it seems like something, if it is removed.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the knots do not come to the member because it is too tight, because of which it is necessary that you loosen it immediately, and let it rest for a while until the knots are untied, and then stretch it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things happen to the patient within twenty years, it is not our fault.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the shoulder is dislocated, and the hands can be placed on the patient's chest, and the collarbones are even, and there is little movement and deformation, and the patient falls asleep on their back; and if this dislocation is restored in thirty or forty years, or in twenty years by chance, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Be cautious that on the back of the hand, and in the wrist, there are few dislocations, and only slight pain comes from it, many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, and if the patient can hold it steady, and holds it firmly in front of him; then he places his hand on the extended toe, and extends the muscles of the broken bones, and places them evenly in the joints, as far as they are well joined; and applies plaster and bandages, if necessary, then he puts a splint according to the size of the foot; and it is wrapped in a fold of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the heel of the foot, near the sole of the plantar bone, I make a dressing of bandages, and instruct the patient to bind the broken bone; and then stretch it with a long bandage, and it is tied, as it should be, if it can be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the hip, then if you can place a splint on it, and another in the foot, if the hand is straight and erect, then the leg will be completely fixed between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture does not occur in either of us, if it is bent, then if you fix it straight, if you can; and with the foot, and if you see that you put a splint on the ankle, and if you lift the fracture with it, and if it does not move; and if the fracture occurs in others, if it is in the index or one of the others, if it is bent, and the other is fixed, and the hand is straight, which is good, or you put on a splint, as much as possible, or you put on an ankle brace, if you can; and be careful in the restoration and the position of the abscess, and see what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the joint is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration is done by reattaching the ligaments that were torn, and the other part is left alone.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient feels pain in their face, then they extend each muscle of their limb evenly; and it is when the break occurs in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the joint, then one or more of the ligaments will be torn in the direction of the point, and the others will be left alone.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And as it approaches the joint, and therefore the ligaments of the joint are relaxed, and the extension is lost; then place the bone evenly in your two hands, according to its natural figure, and then apply the splint, and the bandage, and do not let it move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has become inflamed, if you let it rest, then return to your work and your care; the bandage is made in part manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap it around the brace I bend doubled in II or III, and remove any excess, then twist the leg as far as the heel reaches the root of the nail, and place one end of the string between the thigh and the leg, loosening the joint of the knee; then twist the leg and the thigh with the bend, and put on the brace, and put an eyelet in the leg bone; then place the leather between the leg and the thigh to make it even, and then start tying three or four turns around the brace; and as you add more turns of the brace, the string becomes less tight; then take out the two ends of the string that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and at the third eyelet that is on the brace, until you see the petticoat; the string, if it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, and if it does not swell or change appearance in any other way.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it moves, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that prick, if it can be, then it can; and if not, then it can cut the bone and draw out; and the cure, as we have said, depending on how healthy it is.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never has the cheek been broken once, when I put it in its place, as we do with the arm and shoulder; however, in the restoration that is made, it does not click on the patient's pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And advises that the cheek is restored in L years, or less than less, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the right knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the right knee joint there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, whether it is only a sprain or a puncture, and it comes to all wounds and hurts, and it feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is if you put back what has been dislocated as much as possible, until it is assembled and can be; then put the splint, and if you have a round staple, insert it, and draw it tightly, as you should, then reward all the positions we have said for other dislocations, such as apoplexy and other appearances; if you put back whatever is necessary for each accident, as much as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is sometimes called "right" but not "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it breaks all equally as the arm does, and for this reason the restoration is done in the same way as the right arm, and the joints are all turned. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then feel for great pain and see that it is well; then turn slowly.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	1. Then, apply extension and place it evenly; but remember, if the break is ugly, and there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Once you have completed your work, if you have long hair that pricks the leg on both sides and is as long as the leg from the groin to the ankle, and then wrap it around the leg from the knee to the ankle, and tie it tightly, and make sure the leg does not deviate to the right or left, and it is well; and no one has caused pain in the leg, and it was from the hair, and he puts it on the leg to prevent movement, and it is properly made at the fracture or wound; and shake each leg every day to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones of the shoulder
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but the bones of the shoulder never break and must be very strong, and they only crack in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the bones of the shoulder break and you see them pushing against each other, if they are so thin that they touch the ground, just like when you are flying, then now put your hand on the cheek, lift the bone as much as it can in its place, then press it until it feels firm in its place; then put the splint and staples, and make a small pillow under the shoulder blade, then draw it towards the shoulder, then wrap the bandage around, and other things that you know.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bone is not healed, for you will find that the bones are broken and dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are two broken bones, if they are repaired, as we have said, then place a steel on one of the breaks according to its length; and make the other end larger, then place a pulley on that uneven joint that I mentioned, and tighten it evenly; and if there are II or III, or more, broken bones, then place one steel on each according to its quantity, wound around in one direction of lin, and tighten the pulley away from the joint of the pectoral muscle so that it sticks well. And if it is hanging down from the chest of the pectoral muscle, then it will stick well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	It is necessary that you do not ignore the other things I have said about other injuries, as soon as we have said them; and treat each accident as we have advised.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the small finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's bone is broken, if it is set in place, then it leans towards the side of the small finger, and is held by the thigh; then fill the nature of the wound with cloth, and put it as high as possible; then bring the woman to bed, and gently bend the hip a little at a time, and as soon as the nature comes into the wound, return the bone with the cloth; and when she sees blood, if the cloth is soaked, and when she has stopped bleeding, put it back on, and leave it in seven days or more: if the fracture is restored, and you see it, take a bucket of water, and tie a cord to the nipple, and blow all the water into the nature; then suck out of the cord forms, as long as the water is filled with cloth: the nature will return to the fracture; then fill it with cloth, and leave it without any more days, as long as it is healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the woman, if it is repaired as we have said in the elbow of the horse; and these fractures are not hidden from him who sets the bone and dresses it, and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies in more ways than one the right direction of the restoration: understand the directions.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the angle, when it is broken, take an ostrich's beak and bite the angle; then wrap it around, and leave three turns or in the opposite direction, and it will be cured quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of a fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, whether it is the bone of the shoulder or the helper, or seeming, that they are now healthy, if those wounds that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is that it re-bleeds, if you have nothing else, then continue to restore the fracture in the same hour, or the next day, if the patient does not die.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the patient does not die, then leave the restoration for the next day, as long as the patient is calm and does not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause other accidents to happen.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone is broken, it is located at the point discovered, so you should place it lightly in your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension is not easy to make with your hands, if the ramus has this instrument which is of iron, which is seven or eight fingers long, and the angle is according to the size of the wound; and for this reason, it is necessary to make three or four, according to how much work there is in each case of fracture; and it should be thin and a little large, so that it does not slip with the compression on the member of your hand, and should also be ahead, and large at the front end.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	The first line of the text is translated as: "And it is called 'palinchage', because it is intended that the shoulders be placed on the top of the bone of the shoulder; and the bandage once, as much as it rises, and is equal to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	The second line of the text is translated as: "And if the fracture is subtle, and the bandages cannot well hold the bone, then it is necessary to cover the top of the bone with the bandage, as long as the bandages have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	The third line of the text is translated as: "And if you do not bring the bone back, as we have said, if the top covers an instrument that is suitable for your power, or sharp or stronger, then relieve this which is causing pain in the bone with roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is re-set, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, seek medical attention immediately, as there may be a problem with their natural joint.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you continue until it is in its place, then dress the wound with a piece of black, lint-like material, and make sure it is clean and not oily, as it can cause irritation and infection; then administer medications as needed after setting the bone, and leave the wound open, covering it completely according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound does not become tight with the fracture; many have had this problem, and have caused the patient's death or corrosion, and have always caused more strain and more sores on other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, if we have said so, and you feel pain in the leg, but cannot manage to put on bandages; then wrap the leg with cloth, cut off the loose parts, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound has healed completely, and if you have used antiseptic cream on it, and you have applied a salve to relieve pain, which is a safe and effective remedy, then proceed with the following steps.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary to stretch the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is sore and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the member be aligned in some way so that the bow can be applied lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they persist, and it cannot be held steady but moves away from the bow, you must try to reduce the fracture with a splint, and all those pieces that cause pain must be covered with the bandage.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If an abscess comes to the knee, or any other form of infection, if you are able to treat it, according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If the bone is broken and exposed through the skin, as if it were the bone of the elbow or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if it is not treated immediately, because many times death comes after 20 years or 30, then the wound is left to heal on its own; and if it does not heal, then treat the wound.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The first sentence to translate is "des brus qui viennent sortre la sodure". The translation is
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of the fracture, even when it is near the joint, and it is a shame to see the limb in such a position; and by chance, it cannot make the limb its natural size.

dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The dislocated limb after the injury
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the dislocated form of the limb is deformed, it does not belong to its natural nature: if one does not believe the fools who say that the whole bone must be broken at once, and all others have done this in our land; and these fractures are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and by chance the death occurs; however, if the wounds and torments are fresh, and if they are washed with hot water or herbs that soften, as if with warm viscam, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a mollifying ointment, as if it were well made, and I take the muscle of viscam, and cook it with fat of linseed or oil of saffron, and apply it thus; or I take fat figs, and crush them with fish of collarel, and similar medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is there a stop to the node when it is continued and long with wet hands.

And if the tortuosity is awakened and hardened, as with a wound, and there is need for the bone to be fused, then it comes to cope with the covering of the bone, in the incision subtle and lightly; and put on bandages and study in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it comes now to bring sensation to the arm.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, and it becomes inflamed, and by chance we reset it on the shoulder; because it does not move to the ear when it is inflamed: many times brought pain and other pains; always, when this happens, I make the patient healthier, then let him, as long as the abscess is not healed; then warm and oily ointment is applied to the limb, then it is gently reset, and each member is cured as it was cured in its shoulder.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters of shoulder dislocations by the pieces of bone.
des mandibules	by the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are two ways for the mandibles to be dislocated: either a small piece of bone is missing from one or both of the jaws, and it is softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and causing saliva to drip from the mouth, which cannot be held or closed, and wrapping around the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it can return to its original position through various adjustments.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	1. And if it is complete and accomplished, then you should reset it as soon as possible without force; in such a way that the physician marks the shoulder of the patient, and cuts the roots of the dislocation of the lower jawbone at the corner of the mouth, where the dislocation is located; and the other two hands are deformed to make them equal; and instruct the patient to smooth and move their jaws and all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	2. And the teeth are placed evenly, as they should be in his mouth.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	3. And if the jaw is reset, then it should be done gently, just like the lower jaws when the teeth are aligned, using warm and oily ointments as much as possible; do not force it to be reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are properly returned to their place and the patient's mouth feels well tightened, if you put soft flannels moistened with oil of rosemary and wax on it, then gently tie the legs; let the patient sleep on his back, and his head between two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor strain himself to breathe, but lightly chew on meat as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws; then take what you see lightly, and do not force your mouth open with the tongue and lips, as long as the jaw is well fixed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be reinserted at once in an hour, and are not converted to their original shape, then if fevers and customary colds come on, and by chance the abdomen becomes distended, and by chance vomiting of pure bile occurs.

de la forcelle	of force.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be dislodged from the cost, due to the continuation of the effort and the pain, and it is never loosened at the end, and it is felt to be so.

de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: either it is dislocated at the head of the humerus; or at the shoulder; or at the elbow, and this happens rarely; or it does not dislocate at all from the shoulder, but rather from the nerves; and more often it dislocates towards the humerus, especially in those who have little strength, because they fall very far; in those who have enough strength, they fall a short distance and return a short distance.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they strike or crush their shoulder, and stretch out the shoulder with an abscess, and take care to have it dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Then examine the dislocations as they move towards the axilla, and make a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one; you will find a gap between them, and at the head of the shoulder, you will find the axilla at the top of the shoulder, just like some holes; and it cannot bring its hand to its eye, nor move with any movements; and if it is dislocated high, if it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the axilla; and this way of dislocation is not easy to return, when it is new, or when the patient is a child.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister gently places the hand on the shoulder of the patient, then spreads your fingers wide, and gently moves the joint upwards towards the elbow; the minister gently places the hand, extends it upwards, and places it beside the shoulder; if it happens quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not happen as we have said in our hands just after, then it is necessary that the patient be dipped in warm water; the hand is gently warmed and soothed, like a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in warm water, and is applied; then the patient's shoulder is soaked, and a piece of linen is placed on the back, not too wet nor too dry, then the heel of the foot is placed on the stool, and the main vein is gently stroked, and the hand of the patient is drawn up; other ministers will touch the patient's shoulder to prevent it from moving; this shoulder now returns, and if you see that it follows in this manner: then the present home which is larger than the shoulder is dressed; it is turned towards the cost, and the arm is placed below the shoulder, and the shoulder is lifted, so that the shoulder hangs downwards; other ministers then draw the hand upwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, and there is nothing heavy with it, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reduction is also done another way: and it is like this: and it is like the long rib in the earth, whose head is also returned as if it were a pistil, and not too big or too rough; then it is put back into the shoulder, but if it has twisted too much, and the shoulder is stretched out, then the hand is formed on the other side, and the joint returns to its place immediately; and if it does not return in all these things that we have said, then this cure is made: take two thick braces of the left arm and four thin ones, which have the chief entered from the front of the forearm, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie the head of the shoulder that was not bleeding, then place it in the palm of the hand; extend some arms over the long shoulder, and the helper over the shoulder of the arm, then place the arm at the elbow of an awl of large size, and extend the hands on the other side, and leave the chest hanging from another part: the joint was now relieved.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in whatever way that may be, if you happen to put the palm of your hand a linen thread as even as possible, then place a sprinkle of flour on the mill with incense and wool all over the shoulder and around, then tighten the thread on the palm again, and turn the lace on the sprinkle, and wrap your hand around the arm at its collar, and let the hands remain still.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	The patient should drink little by little, as the limb is comfortable, because it heals faster; then drink more after the first seven days or weeks, and move it; and if it is tight and not softened, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	If the joint is swollen due to moisture or another reason, and it has not subsided after three days, then it is necessary to apply a cauterization at the third position, as shown in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you follow all these steps, and after seven weeks, the joint still does not hold and cannot lift the arm forward, it means that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is compressed or extended or softened; and it means that the joint will never return to its original position.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the toe, and the ankles, or the heel, if it is made by force, and stretching of hands, and it is treated at another time; and it is cured when it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing comes pain in the limb, and later in movement, if the patient uses cold water many times, as long as that pain is not relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dear dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It is said that the costly joint is dislocated at many points, and those points return; and it is dislocated from all parts, even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not well set because it is seen and felt well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the male member with the female, if you see it open wide.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is weak, and cannot grip the arm, nor touch the shoulder with anything.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it always with the thumb and index finger, because if you do not reset it, it would be painful to return; and by chance, it cannot be reset at all, even when it is in the groin; rather than other dislocations, and it causes more pain, and by chance, it comes to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the resetting is necessary when it is, if it can be returned, that you extend your hand to your two hands; and the arms are expanded, and the hands are pulled according to the chest, from the outside and inside, and tie the joint with your fingers together, or at the root of the palm, as it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and proud of the root of the palm tree that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to the shoulder, then apply strong extension; and if two people extend the arm, and hold it with two people, so that it does not move at extension, then turn the arm in each part, then wrap a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the patient feels the joint at the shoulder, if there is no oil to lubricate the joint, then bend the joint as much as it can; and when it returns to the shoulder, put a dry cloth with a piece of beef dripping on it, and form the arm at the bottom of the injured limb, and leave some fingers, then let go.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	When the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if it does not move, and it is left; and if you see that the joint does not tighten well, then repeat the application and the joint, and leave for a while until it is firmly fixed; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If the patient feels pain after the reduction of the joint, and it becomes quiet, if it is bathed and gently rubbed, and pressed until it is calmed; or you put on the joint a fat sheep's wool dressing, then leave it for one night and the bone, and let the bone enter or bath; and when it is awake, gently rub the joint, then remove the wool dressing, and then enter or bath; and repeat two or three times until it is healthy; and if you see, if you put on fat sheep's wool moistened with butter, and press it; if it returns to its original position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand dislocates, and the return is lighter than other joints. It is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately, while it is dislocated, unless the arm is shortened or there is an abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement. Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then he should place his hand on top of his arm on the table, and he should see if his hand fits into this appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it does not return now, then it is well if it does not, since the relief of the plaster does not cause pain. Let him continue to try again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not put the hand in the arm after any time, since the dislocation is painful; and if the hands are not softened, and nothing can be stretched at all: then you should know that the nerves are wounded, or the artery; if there is no other engine than to strain with fire cautery, and by chance it does not work any other way.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hands are at the elbow, if they are placed on the probe that we have mentioned, then it is tightened and left for a while, then it is loosened and left alone.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved well, and there is no swelling, if the hot poultice of wool is applied, and the area is friced as much as possible when it is dry.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of both hands.

des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The shoulder joints and the shoulder blade joints are only dislocations, not like other joints; and the shoulder joint is divided into four parts: superior and inferior, front and back; and more superior ones, and less on the front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of a dislocation is that when the injured leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer and more open, and the injured knee cannot double its joint at fire; and this is the one that is deformed due to abscess compression, because the head of the thigh comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who comes to the forge, if this accident is contrary to these fronts.

And the signs of him who came to the front, if they are well in his leg according to the completion; however, do not double the gentle sensations with pain, and if you see it moving, if it cannot before, and retains its urine, and enflames the anus, and when he goes, if it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes. Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption. The second line of the text translates to: "And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry and return the joint, it will be tense and deformed, and the limb will be bent to the left and right; by chance, if it returns, and there is no other cure.

Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.

de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it should not be pulled downwards or to the side, but rather behind.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez. de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the big toe
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The big toe is never used, and it is never completely dislocated, and it is bent and twisted.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the hands should be light, and it should be gently extended when it is only tense.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, and before reaching the part where it is swollen: the hands should be light, and it should be gently extended when it is only tense. Then sit the patient on their right side, and pull the leg with your hand; then take the foot in your left hand, and twice lift it up, and hold it at the top; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and lifting the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, if it does not return, continue the treatment, as it will return; and if it cannot return again, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and hold the knee firmly on the ground between the thighs, and bend the leg; then mark the other assistants with the knee, and extend the foot to their hands or to the patient's elbow; then extend all the assistants equally, and the patient should be between the knees of the ankle to hold the ankle; then place the dislocation in your hands, and have the other assistants mark the healthy leg at the back, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When the dislocation occurs, if it is treated with plaster and bandages, and the limb is formed, and the patient lies down on the leg, and covers the nerves that are at the ankle joint, so that the ligaments do not become too tight; then it is left to stay for two to three days, and if the ligaments tighten, then it is loosened; then it is removed at the end of the third or fourth day, and the patient is allowed to walk on it with the aid of crutches for four days; and if the dislocation does not improve, it is a sign that the treatment has not been successful.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound becomes inflamed and comes, if it is necessary to calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy.
des dois	Of two things, one is that the
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	If both are dislocated, and they are able to be extended gently in the work, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way painful to the shoulder or joint, and it comes that you must hold the patient on their side or on their stomach, then place your foot on the part where the joints open, then press with your foot on this part until it returns; and when it is straight, if it does not open, then place a table under the head of the shoulder at the shoulder blade, then form the foot, and leave it there, then remove it; and let them rest, as long as they are healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When wound and dislocation occur together, and it is seen that the wound is being restored, many times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your treatment, whether you are skilled in the art and have used it for a long time, and whether you are pitiful and merciful and slow, do not be presumptuous; and begin with soothing remedies for abscesses, and let the patient hold onto the hand of God; and when you see hope for health, reset the member to its place immediately, even if the abscess is painful and vigorous; and when the member is at its place, apply soothing remedies for abscesses, and cure the wound, as it is necessary, with desiccants; and if there is a break with dislocation, and the bones are small, then the bones, and do as I have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into the path of despair, according to what I have said, because this is according to your creator, and for the wisdom of your arm and heart.
